      <p><b>Colombia</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ʌ/: 'u' in 'cut'">ʌ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-Colombia-pronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/63/En-Colombia-pronunciation.ogg" class="internal" title="En-Colombia-pronunciation.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">kə-<span style="font-size:90%">LUM</span>-bee-ə</i></a>, <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span></span>-/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">-⁠LOM-</i></a>;<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> <small>Spanish:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[koˈlombja]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Es-colombia.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/de/Es-colombia.ogg" class="internal" title="Es-colombia.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>), officially the <b>Republic of Colombia</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[a]</a></sup> is a country in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> with <a href="/wiki/Insular_region_of_Colombia" title="Insular region of Colombia">territories</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>. It is bounded on the north by the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, the northwest by <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>, the south by <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, the east by <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, the southeast by <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, and the west by the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>. Colombia is composed of 32 <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Colombia" title="Departments of Colombia">departments</a> and the Capital District of <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogotá">Bogotá</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Colombia_by_population" title="List of cities in Colombia by population">country's largest city</a>. It covers an area of 1,418,748 square kilometres (547,782&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), with a population of 50 million. Colombia's rich <a href="/wiki/Cultural_heritage" title="Cultural heritage">cultural heritage</a> reflects influences by various Amerindian civilisations, European settlement, forced African labour, and <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Colombia" title="Immigration to Colombia">immigration</a> from Europe and the Middle East. <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> is the nation's <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>, besides which <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Colombia" title="Languages of Colombia">over 70 languages</a> are spoken. </p>
      <p>Colombia has been inhabited by various <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Colombia" title="Indigenous peoples in Colombia">indigenous peoples</a> since at least 12,000 BCE, including the <a href="/wiki/Muisca" title="Muisca">Muisca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quimbaya_civilization" title="Quimbaya civilization">Quimbaya</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Tairona" title="Tairona">Tairona</a>. The Spanish landed first in La Guajira in 1499 and by the mid-16th century <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">colonized</a> parts of the region, establishing the <a href="/wiki/New_Kingdom_of_Granada" title="New Kingdom of Granada">New Kingdom of Granada</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogotá">Santafé de Bogotá</a> as its capital. <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">Independence</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> was achieved in 1810, with what is now Colombia emerging as the <a href="/wiki/United_Provinces_of_New_Granada" title="United Provinces of New Granada">United Provinces of New Granada</a>. The new nation experimented with federalism as the <a href="/wiki/Granadine_Confederation" title="Granadine Confederation">Granadine Confederation</a> (1858), and then the <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_Colombia" title="United States of Colombia">United States of Colombia</a> (1863), before the Republic of Colombia was finally declared in 1886. <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_Panama_from_Colombia" title="Separation of Panama from Colombia">Panama seceded</a> in 1903, leading to Colombia's present borders. Beginning in the 1960s, the country has suffered from an asymmetric low-intensity <a href="/wiki/Colombian_armed_conflict_(1964%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="Colombian armed conflict (1964–present)">armed conflict</a> and political violence, both of which escalated in the 1990s. Since 2005, there has been significant improvement in security, stability, and rule of law, as well as unprecedented economic growth and development.<sup id="cite_ref-Enough_Already!_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Enough_Already!-15">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Colombia's_GDP_growth_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombia's_GDP_growth-16">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Colombia is one of the world's seventeen <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">megadiverse countries</a>, and has the second-highest level of <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_of_Colombia" title="Biodiversity of Colombia">biodiversity</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Biodiversity_of_Colombia_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Biodiversity_of_Colombia-17">[15]</a></sup> Its territory encompasses <a href="/wiki/Amazon_natural_region" title="Amazon natural region">Amazon rainforest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andean_natural_region" title="Andean natural region">highlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orinoqu%C3%ADa_natural_region" title="Orinoquía natural region">grasslands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tatacoa_Desert" title="Tatacoa Desert">deserts</a>, and it is the only country in South America with coastlines and islands along both <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_natural_region" title="Caribbean natural region">Atlantic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pacific/Choc%C3%B3_natural_region" title="Pacific/Chocó natural region">Pacific</a> oceans. Colombia is a member of major global and regional organisations including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a>, the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">OAS</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Alliance" title="Pacific Alliance">Pacific Alliance</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Andean_Community" title="Andean Community">Andean Community</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> Global Partner. Its <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Colombia" title="Economy of Colombia">diversified economy</a> is the third-largest in South America, with macroeconomic stability and favorable long-term growth prospects.<sup id="cite_ref-GDP_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GDP-18">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-strongmacroeconomicmanagement_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strongmacroeconomicmanagement-19">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">
       <input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2> 
      <p>The name "Colombia" is derived from the last name of the Italian navigator <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> (<a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <i lang="it">Cristoforo Colombo</i>, Spanish: <i lang="es">Cristóbal Colón</i>). It was conceived as a reference to all of the New World.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> The name was later adopted by the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">Republic of Colombia</a> of 1819, formed from the territories of the old <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Granada" title="Viceroyalty of New Granada">Viceroyalty of New Granada</a> (modern-day Colombia, Panama, Venezuela, Ecuador, and northwest Brazil).<sup id="cite_ref-LABLAA5_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LABLAA5-21">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>When Venezuela, Ecuador, and <a href="/wiki/Cundinamarca_Department_(1820)" title="Cundinamarca Department (1820)">Cundinamarca</a> came to exist as independent states, the former <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_the_Republic_of_New_Granada" title="Provinces of the Republic of New Granada">Department of Cundinamarca</a> adopted the name "<a href="/wiki/Republic_of_New_Granada" title="Republic of New Granada">Republic of New Granada</a>". New Granada officially changed its name in 1858 to the <a href="/wiki/Granadine_Confederation" title="Granadine Confederation">Granadine Confederation</a>. In 1863 the name was again changed, this time to <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_Colombia" title="United States of Colombia">United States of Colombia</a>, before finally adopting its present name – the Republic of Colombia – in 1886.<sup id="cite_ref-LABLAA5_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LABLAA5-21">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>To refer to this country, the Colombian government uses the terms <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">Colombia</i> and <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">República de Colombia</i>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Colombia" title="History of Colombia">History of Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Colombian_history" title="Timeline of Colombian history">Timeline of Colombian history</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Columbian_era">Pre-Columbian era</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_cultures_of_Colombia" title="Pre-Columbian cultures of Colombia">Pre-Columbian cultures of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Culture_pr%C3%A9colombiennes_en_Colombie.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Culture_pr%C3%A9colombiennes_en_Colombie.png/220px-Culture_pr%C3%A9colombiennes_en_Colombie.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Culture_pr%C3%A9colombiennes_en_Colombie.png/330px-Culture_pr%C3%A9colombiennes_en_Colombie.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Culture_pr%C3%A9colombiennes_en_Colombie.png/440px-Culture_pr%C3%A9colombiennes_en_Colombie.png 2x" data-file-width="646" data-file-height="745"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Culture_pr%C3%A9colombiennes_en_Colombie.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Location map of the pre-Columbian cultures of Colombia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Owing to its location, the present territory of Colombia was a corridor of early human civilization from <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amazon_basin" title="Amazon basin">Amazon basin</a>. The oldest archaeological finds are from the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pubenza_archaeological_site&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pubenza archaeological site (page does not exist)">Pubenza</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Totumo_archaeological_site&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="El Totumo archaeological site (page does not exist)">El Totumo</a> sites in the Magdalena Valley 100 kilometres (62&nbsp;mi) southwest of Bogotá.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup> These sites date from the <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Indians" title="Paleo-Indians">Paleoindian</a> period (18,000–8000&nbsp;BCE). At <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Hormiga_archaeological_site" title="Puerto Hormiga archaeological site">Puerto Hormiga</a> and other sites, traces from the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Archaic_period_in_South_America&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Archaic period in South America (page does not exist)">Archaic Period</a> (~8000–2000&nbsp;BCE) have been found. Vestiges indicate that there was also early occupation in the regions of <a href="/wiki/El_Abra" title="El Abra">El Abra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tequendama" title="Tequendama">Tequendama</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cundinamarca_Department_(1820)" title="Cundinamarca Department (1820)">Cundinamarca</a>. The oldest pottery discovered in the Americas, found at <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Jacinto_archaeological_site&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="San Jacinto archaeological site (page does not exist)">San Jacinto</a>, dates to 5000–4000&nbsp;BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Indigenous people inhabited the territory that is now Colombia by 12,500&nbsp;BCE. Nomadic <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherer</a> tribes at the <a href="/wiki/El_Abra" title="El Abra">El Abra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tibit%C3%B3" title="Tibitó">Tibitó</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tequendama" title="Tequendama">Tequendama</a> sites near present-day <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogotá">Bogotá</a> traded with one another and with other cultures from the <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_River" title="Magdalena River">Magdalena River</a> Valley.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup> A site including eight miles of <a href="/wiki/Pictogram" title="Pictogram">pictographs</a> that is under study at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Serran%C3%ADa_de_la_Lindosa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Serranía de la Lindosa (page does not exist)">Serranía de la Lindosa</a> was revealed in November 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup> Their age is suggested as being 12,500 years old (c. 10,480 B.C.) by the anthropologists working on the site because of extinct fauna depicted. That would have been during the earliest known human occupation of the area now known as Colombia. </p>
      <p>Between 5000 and 1000&nbsp;BCE, hunter-gatherer tribes transitioned to agrarian societies; fixed settlements were established, and pottery appeared. Beginning in the 1st millennium BCE, groups of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Amerindians</a> including the <a href="/wiki/Muisca" title="Muisca">Muisca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zen%C3%BA" title="Zenú">Zenú</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quimbaya_civilization" title="Quimbaya civilization">Quimbaya</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tairona" title="Tairona">Tairona</a> developed the political system of <i><a href="/wiki/Cacicazgo" title="Cacicazgo">cacicazgos</a></i> with a pyramidal structure of power headed by <i>caciques</i>. The Muisca inhabited mainly the area of what is now the <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Colombia" title="Departments of Colombia">Departments</a> of <a href="/wiki/Boyac%C3%A1_Department" title="Boyacá Department">Boyacá</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cundinamarca_Department" title="Cundinamarca Department">Cundinamarca</a> high plateau (<i><a href="/wiki/Altiplano_Cundiboyacense" title="Altiplano Cundiboyacense">Altiplano Cundiboyacense</a></i>) where they formed the <a href="/wiki/Muisca_Confederation" title="Muisca Confederation">Muisca Confederation</a>. They farmed maize, potato, quinoa, and cotton, and traded gold, <a href="/wiki/Colombian_emeralds" title="Colombian emeralds">emeralds</a>, blankets, ceramic handicrafts, coca and especially <a href="/wiki/Halite" title="Halite">rock salt</a> with neighboring nations. The Tairona inhabited northern Colombia in the isolated mountain range of <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_de_Santa_Marta" title="Sierra Nevada de Santa Marta">Sierra Nevada de Santa Marta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> The Quimbaya inhabited regions of the <a href="/wiki/Cauca_River" title="Cauca River">Cauca River</a> Valley between the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Occidental_(Colombia)" title="Cordillera Occidental (Colombia)">Western</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Colombia)" title="Cordillera Central (Colombia)">Central</a> Ranges of the Colombian Andes.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup> Most of the Amerindians practiced agriculture and the social structure of each indigenous community was different. Some groups of indigenous people such as the Caribs lived in a state of permanent war, but others had less bellicose attitudes.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_annexation">European annexation</span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Alonso_de_Ojeda" title="Alonso de Ojeda">Alonso de Ojeda</a> (who had sailed with Columbus) reached the <a href="/wiki/Guajira_Peninsula" title="Guajira Peninsula">Guajira Peninsula</a> in 1499.<sup id="cite_ref-LABLAA6_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LABLAA6-29">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup> Spanish explorers, led by <a href="/wiki/Rodrigo_de_Bastidas" title="Rodrigo de Bastidas">Rodrigo de Bastidas</a>, made the first exploration of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Basin" title="Caribbean Basin">Caribbean coast</a> in 1500.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> navigated near the Caribbean in 1502.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup> In 1508, <a href="/wiki/Vasco_N%C3%BA%C3%B1ez_de_Balboa" title="Vasco Núñez de Balboa">Vasco Núñez de Balboa</a> accompanied an expedition to the territory through the region of <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Urab%C3%A1" title="Gulf of Urabá">Gulf of Urabá</a> and they founded the town of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_la_Antigua_del_Dari%C3%A9n" title="Santa María la Antigua del Darién">Santa María la Antigua del Darién</a> in 1510, the first stable settlement on the continent. <sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[Note 2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Santa_Marta" title="Santa Marta">Santa Marta</a> was founded in 1525,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[32]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Colombia" title="Cartagena, Colombia">Cartagena</a> in 1533.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[33]</a></sup> Spanish <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistador</a> <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Quesada" title="Gonzalo Jiménez de Quesada">Gonzalo Jiménez de Quesada</a> led an expedition to the interior in April 1536, and christened the districts through which he passed "<a href="/wiki/New_Kingdom_of_Granada" title="New Kingdom of Granada">New Kingdom of Granada</a>". In August 1538, he founded provisionally its capital near the Muisca <a href="/wiki/Cacicazgo" title="Cacicazgo">cacicazgo</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bacat%C3%A1" title="Bacatá">Bacatá</a>, and named it "Santa Fe". The name soon acquired a suffix and was called Santa Fe de Bogotá.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[35]</a></sup> Two other notable journeys by early conquistadors to the interior took place in the same period. <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_de_Belalc%C3%A1zar" title="Sebastián de Belalcázar">Sebastián de Belalcázar</a>, conqueror of <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a>, traveled north and founded <a href="/wiki/Cali" title="Cali">Cali</a>, in 1536, and <a href="/wiki/Popay%C3%A1n" title="Popayán">Popayán</a>, in 1537;<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[36]</a></sup> from 1536 to 1539, German conquistador <a href="/wiki/Nikolaus_Federmann" title="Nikolaus Federmann">Nikolaus Federmann</a> crossed the <a href="/wiki/Orinoqu%C3%ADa_Natural_Region,_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Orinoquía Natural Region, Colombia">Llanos Orientales</a> and went over the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Oriental_(Colombia)" title="Cordillera Oriental (Colombia)">Cordillera Oriental</a> in a search for <a href="/wiki/El_Dorado" title="El Dorado">El Dorado</a>, the "city of gold".<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[38]</a></sup> The legend and the gold would play a pivotal role in luring the Spanish and other Europeans to New Granada during the 16th and 17th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_conquistadors_in_Colombia" title="List of conquistadors in Colombia">conquistadors</a> made frequent alliances with the enemies of different indigenous communities. <a href="/wiki/Indian_auxiliaries" title="Indian auxiliaries">Indigenous allies</a> were crucial to conquest, as well as to creating and maintaining empire.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[40]</a></sup> Indigenous peoples in New Granada experienced a decline in population due to conquest as well as Eurasian diseases, such as <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a>, to which they had no immunity.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[42]</a></sup> Regarding the land as deserted, the Spanish Crown sold properties to all persons interested in colonised territories, creating large farms and possession of mines.<sup id="cite_ref-TierrasColonia_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TierrasColonia-46">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EconomíaColonial_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EconomíaColonial-47">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-políticaeconómica_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-políticaeconómica-48">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 16th century, the <a href="/wiki/Nautical_science" class="mw-redirect" title="Nautical science">nautical science</a> in Spain reached a great development thanks to numerous scientific figures of the <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_Contrataci%C3%B3n" title="Casa de Contratación">Casa de Contratación</a> and nautical science was an essential pillar of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_ship_development,_1400%E2%80%931600" title="Iberian ship development, 1400–1600">Iberian expansion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Alonso_de_Santa_Cruz_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alonso_de_Santa_Cruz-49">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_exchange">Colonial exchange</span></h3> 
      <p>In 1542, the region of New Granada, along with all other Spanish possessions in South America, became part of the <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_Peru" title="Viceroyalty of Peru">Viceroyalty of Peru</a>, with its capital in <a href="/wiki/Lima" title="Lima">Lima</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[47]</a></sup> In 1547, New Granada became the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Captaincy-General_of_New_Granada&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Captaincy-General of New Granada (page does not exist)">Captaincy-General of New Granada</a> within the viceroyalty. </p>
      <p>In 1549, the <a href="/wiki/Real_Audiencia" title="Real Audiencia">Royal Audiencia</a> was created by a royal decree, and New Granada was ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Audience_of_Santa_Fe_de_Bogot%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Audience of Santa Fe de Bogotá">Royal Audience of Santa Fe de Bogotá</a>, which at that time comprised the provinces of Santa Marta, Rio de San Juan, Popayán, Guayana and Cartagena.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[48]</a></sup> But important decisions were taken from the colony to Spain by the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Indies" title="Council of the Indies">Council of the Indies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Defensa_de_Cartagena_de_Indias_por_la_escuadra_de_D._Blas_de_Lezo,_a%C3%B1o_1741.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Defensa_de_Cartagena_de_Indias_por_la_escuadra_de_D._Blas_de_Lezo%2C_a%C3%B1o_1741.jpg/220px-Defensa_de_Cartagena_de_Indias_por_la_escuadra_de_D._Blas_de_Lezo%2C_a%C3%B1o_1741.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Defensa_de_Cartagena_de_Indias_por_la_escuadra_de_D._Blas_de_Lezo%2C_a%C3%B1o_1741.jpg/330px-Defensa_de_Cartagena_de_Indias_por_la_escuadra_de_D._Blas_de_Lezo%2C_a%C3%B1o_1741.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Defensa_de_Cartagena_de_Indias_por_la_escuadra_de_D._Blas_de_Lezo%2C_a%C3%B1o_1741.jpg/440px-Defensa_de_Cartagena_de_Indias_por_la_escuadra_de_D._Blas_de_Lezo%2C_a%C3%B1o_1741.jpg 2x" data-file-width="795" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Defensa_de_Cartagena_de_Indias_por_la_escuadra_de_D._Blas_de_Lezo,_a%C3%B1o_1741.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An illustration of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cartagena_de_Indias" title="Battle of Cartagena de Indias">Battle of Cartagena de Indias</a>, a major Spanish victory in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_Jenkins%27_Ear" title="War of Jenkins' Ear">War of Jenkins' Ear</a><sup id="cite_ref-BattleofCartagena_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BattleofCartagena-54">[51]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the 16th century, European slave traders had begun to bring <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">enslaved Africans</a> to the Americas. Spain was the only European power that did not establish <a href="/wiki/Factory_(trading_post)" title="Factory (trading post)">factories</a> in Africa to purchase slaves; the Spanish Empire instead relied on the <a href="/wiki/Asiento" class="mw-redirect" title="Asiento">asiento</a> system, awarding merchants from other European nations the license to trade enslaved peoples to their overseas territories.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup> This system brought Africans to Colombia, although many spoke out against the institution.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[Note 3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[Note 4]</a></sup> The indigenous peoples could not be enslaved because they were legally <a href="/wiki/Commoners" class="mw-redirect" title="Commoners">subjects</a> of the Spanish Crown.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[58]</a></sup> To protect the indigenous peoples, several forms of land ownership and regulation were established by the Spanish colonial authorities: <i>resguardos</i>, <i>encomiendas</i> and <i>haciendas</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-TierrasColonia_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TierrasColonia-46">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EconomíaColonial_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EconomíaColonial-47">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-políticaeconómica_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-políticaeconómica-48">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ilustraciones_Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Ilustraciones_Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis.jpg/200px-Ilustraciones_Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Ilustraciones_Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis.jpg/300px-Ilustraciones_Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Ilustraciones_Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis.jpg/400px-Ilustraciones_Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ilustraciones_Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Many intellectual leaders of the independence process participated in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Botanical_Expedition_to_New_Granada" title="Royal Botanical Expedition to New Granada">Royal Botanical Expedition to New Granada</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Granada" title="Viceroyalty of New Granada">Viceroyalty of New Granada</a> was established in 1717, then temporarily removed, and then re-established in 1739. Its capital was Santa Fé de Bogotá. This Viceroyalty included some other provinces of northwestern South America that had previously been under the jurisdiction of the <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">Viceroyalties of New Spain</a> or <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_Peru" title="Viceroyalty of Peru">Peru</a> and correspond mainly to today's Venezuela, Ecuador, and Panama. So, Bogotá became one of the principal administrative centers of the Spanish possessions in the New World, along with <a href="/wiki/Lima" title="Lima">Lima</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>, though it remained somewhat backward compared to those two cities in several economic and logistical ways.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a> declared war <a href="/wiki/War_of_Jenkins_Ear" class="mw-redirect" title="War of Jenkins Ear">on Spain</a> in 1739, and the city of Cartagena quckly became a top target for the British. A massive British expeditionary force was dispatched to capture the city, but after initial inroads devastating outbreaks of disease crippled their numbers and the British were forced to withdraw. The battle became one of Spain's most decisive victories in the conflict, and secured Spanish dominance in the Caribbean until the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BattleofCartagena_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BattleofCartagena-54">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 18th-century priest, botanist and mathematician <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis" title="José Celestino Mutis">José Celestino Mutis</a> was delegated by Viceroy <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Caballero_y_G%C3%B3ngora" title="Antonio Caballero y Góngora">Antonio Caballero y Góngora</a> to conduct an inventory of the nature of New Granada. Started in 1783, this became known as the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Botanical_Expedition_to_New_Granada" title="Royal Botanical Expedition to New Granada">Royal Botanical Expedition to New Granada</a>. It classified plants and wildlife, and founded the first astronomical observatory in the city of Santa Fe de Bogotá.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[62]</a></sup> In July 1801 the Prussian scientist <a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt" title="Alexander von Humboldt">Alexander von Humboldt</a> reached Santa Fe de Bogotá where he met with Mutis. In addition, historical figures in the process of independence in New Granada emerged from the expedition as the astronomer <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Jos%C3%A9_de_Caldas" title="Francisco José de Caldas">Francisco José de Caldas</a>, the scientist <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Antonio_Zea" title="Francisco Antonio Zea">Francisco Antonio Zea</a>, the zoologist <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Tadeo_Lozano" title="Jorge Tadeo Lozano">Jorge Tadeo Lozano</a> and the painter <a href="/wiki/Salvador_Rizo" title="Salvador Rizo">Salvador Rizo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Batalla_de_Boyaca_de_Martin_Tovar_y_Tovar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Batalla_de_Boyaca_de_Martin_Tovar_y_Tovar.jpg/220px-Batalla_de_Boyaca_de_Martin_Tovar_y_Tovar.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Batalla_de_Boyaca_de_Martin_Tovar_y_Tovar.jpg/330px-Batalla_de_Boyaca_de_Martin_Tovar_y_Tovar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Batalla_de_Boyaca_de_Martin_Tovar_y_Tovar.jpg/440px-Batalla_de_Boyaca_de_Martin_Tovar_y_Tovar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1654" data-file-height="1122"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Batalla_de_Boyaca_de_Martin_Tovar_y_Tovar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Boyac%C3%A1" title="Battle of Boyacá">Battle of Boyacá</a> was the decisive battle that ensured success of the <a href="/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar%27s_campaign_to_liberate_New_Granada" title="Bolívar's campaign to liberate New Granada">liberation campaign of New Granada.</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since the beginning of the periods of conquest and colonization, there were several rebel movements against Spanish rule, but most were either crushed or remained too weak to change the overall situation. The last one that sought outright independence from Spain sprang up around 1810 and culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Colombian Declaration of Independence">Colombian Declaration of Independence</a>, issued on 20 July 1810, the day that is now celebrated as the nation's Independence Day.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[65]</a></sup> This movement followed the independence of <a href="/wiki/St._Domingue" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Domingue">St. Domingue</a> (present-day Haiti) in 1804, which provided some support to an eventual leader of this rebellion: <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a>. <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Paula_Santander" title="Francisco de Paula Santander">Francisco de Paula Santander</a> also would play a decisive role.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[68]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ProvinciaSocorro.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/ProvinciaSocorro.jpg/150px-ProvinciaSocorro.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/ProvinciaSocorro.jpg/225px-ProvinciaSocorro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ce/ProvinciaSocorro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="263" data-file-height="322"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ProvinciaSocorro.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Socorro_Province" title="Socorro Province">Socorro Province</a> was the site of the <a href="/wiki/Revolt_of_the_Comuneros_(New_Granada)" title="Revolt of the Comuneros (New Granada)">genesis</a> of the independence process.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A movement was initiated by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Nari%C3%B1o" title="Antonio Nariño">Antonio Nariño</a>, who opposed Spanish centralism and led the opposition against the <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty" title="Viceroyalty">Viceroyalty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[69]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Colombia" title="Cartagena, Colombia">Cartagena</a> became independent in November 1811.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[70]</a></sup> In 1811 the <a href="/wiki/United_Provinces_of_New_Granada" title="United Provinces of New Granada">United Provinces of New Granada</a> were proclaimed, headed by <a href="/wiki/Camilo_Torres_Tenorio" title="Camilo Torres Tenorio">Camilo Torres Tenorio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[72]</a></sup> The emergence of two distinct ideological currents among the patriots (<a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">centralism</a>) gave rise to a period of <a href="/wiki/Patria_Boba" class="mw-redirect" title="Patria Boba">instability</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[73]</a></sup> Shortly after the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> ended, <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferdinand VII">Ferdinand VII</a>, recently restored to the throne in Spain, unexpectedly decided <a href="/wiki/Spanish_reconquest_of_New_Granada" title="Spanish reconquest of New Granada">to send military forces</a> to retake most of northern South America. The viceroyalty was restored under the command of <a href="/wiki/Juan_S%C3%A1mano" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan Sámano">Juan Sámano</a>, whose regime punished those who participated in the patriotic movements, ignoring the political nuances of the <a href="/wiki/Junta_(Spanish_American_Independence)" title="Junta (Spanish American Independence)">juntas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[74]</a></sup> The retribution stoked renewed rebellion, which, combined with a weakened Spain, made possible a successful rebellion led by the Venezuelan-born <a href="/wiki/Military_career_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Military career of Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a>, who finally proclaimed <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">independence</a> in 1819.<sup id="cite_ref-Historia_ilustrada_de_Colombia_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historia_ilustrada_de_Colombia-80">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[76]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Royalist_(Spanish_American_Independence)" class="mw-redirect" title="Royalist (Spanish American Independence)">pro-Spanish resistance</a> was defeated in 1822 in the present territory of Colombia and in 1823 in Venezuela.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The territory of the Viceroyalty of New Granada became the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">Republic of Colombia</a>, organized as a <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Gran_Colombia" title="Subdivisions of Gran Colombia">union of the current territories</a> of Colombia, Panama, Ecuador, Venezuela, parts of Guyana and Brazil and north of <a href="/wiki/Mara%C3%B1%C3%B3n_River" title="Marañón River">Marañón River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[80]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_C%C3%BAcuta" title="Congress of Cúcuta">Congress of Cúcuta</a> in 1821 adopted a <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Constitution_of_1821" title="Colombian Constitution of 1821">constitution</a> for the new Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[82]</a></sup> Simón Bolívar became the first <a href="/wiki/President_of_Colombia" title="President of Colombia">President of Colombia</a>, and Francisco de Paula Santander was made <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_Colombia" title="Vice President of Colombia">Vice President</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[83]</a></sup> However, the new republic was unstable and three countries emerged from the collapse of <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">Gran Colombia</a> in 1830 (New Granada, Ecuador and Venezuela).<sup id="cite_ref-EtHisColombia_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EtHisColombia-89">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GranColombiaNuevaGranada_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GranColombiaNuevaGranada-90">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cambios_territoriales_de_Colombia.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Cambios_territoriales_de_Colombia.gif/220px-Cambios_territoriales_de_Colombia.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Cambios_territoriales_de_Colombia.gif/330px-Cambios_territoriales_de_Colombia.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Cambios_territoriales_de_Colombia.gif/440px-Cambios_territoriales_de_Colombia.gif 2x" data-file-width="1082" data-file-height="1154"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cambios_territoriales_de_Colombia.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Formation of the present Colombia since the <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Granada" title="Viceroyalty of New Granada">Viceroyalty of New Granada</a>'s independence from the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Colombia was the first <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitutional government">constitutional government</a> in South America,<sup id="cite_ref-HistoriaConstitucional_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistoriaConstitucional-91">[86]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Liberal_Party" title="Colombian Liberal Party">Liberal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Conservative_Party" title="Colombian Conservative Party">Conservative</a> parties, founded in 1848 and 1849, respectively, are two of the oldest surviving political parties in the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[87]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">Slavery</a> was abolished in the country in 1851.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Internal political and territorial divisions led to the dissolution of <a href="/wiki/Gran_Colombia" title="Gran Colombia">Gran Colombia</a> in 1830.<sup id="cite_ref-EtHisColombia_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EtHisColombia-89">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GranColombiaNuevaGranada_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GranColombiaNuevaGranada-90">[85]</a></sup> The so-called "<a href="/wiki/Cundinamarca_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Cundinamarca Province">Department of Cundinamarca</a>" adopted the name "<a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_New_Granada" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of the New Granada">New Granada</a>", which it kept until 1858 when it became the "Confederación Granadina" (<a href="/wiki/Granadine_Confederation" title="Granadine Confederation">Granadine Confederation</a>). After a <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Civil_War_(1860%E2%80%931862)" title="Colombian Civil War (1860–1862)">two-year civil war</a> in 1863, the "<a href="/wiki/United_States_of_Colombia" title="United States of Colombia">United States of Colombia</a>" was created, lasting until 1886, when the country finally became known as the Republic of Colombia.<sup id="cite_ref-HistoriaConstitucional_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistoriaConstitucional-91">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[90]</a></sup> Internal divisions remained between the bipartisan political forces, occasionally igniting very bloody civil wars, the most significant being the <a href="/wiki/Thousand_Days%27_War" title="Thousand Days' War">Thousand Days' War</a> (1899–1902).<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[91]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span></h3> 
      <p>The United States of America's intentions to influence the area (especially the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">Panama Canal</a> construction and control)<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[92]</a></sup> led to the <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_Panama_from_Colombia" title="Separation of Panama from Colombia">separation of the Department of Panama</a> in 1903 and the establishment of it as a nation.<sup id="cite_ref-SeparationofPanama_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SeparationofPanama-98">[93]</a></sup> The United States paid Colombia $25,000,000 in 1921, seven years after completion of the canal, for redress of President <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Roosevelt</a>'s role in the creation of Panama, and Colombia recognized Panama under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Thomson%E2%80%93Urrutia_Treaty" title="Thomson–Urrutia Treaty">Thomson–Urrutia Treaty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[94]</a></sup> Colombia and Peru went to <a href="/wiki/Leticia_Incident" title="Leticia Incident">war</a> because of territory disputes far in the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_basin" title="Amazon basin">Amazon basin</a>. The war ended with a peace deal brokered by the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>. The League finally awarded the disputed area to Colombia in June 1934.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[95]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bogotazo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Bogotazo.jpg/220px-Bogotazo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Bogotazo.jpg/330px-Bogotazo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/57/Bogotazo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="391" data-file-height="244"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bogotazo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Bogotazo" title="Bogotazo">Bogotazo</a> in 1948
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Soon after, Colombia achieved some degree of political stability, which was interrupted by a bloody conflict that took place between the late 1940s and the early 1950s, a period known as <i><a href="/wiki/La_Violencia" title="La Violencia">La Violencia</a></i> ("The Violence"). Its cause was mainly mounting tensions between the two leading political parties, which subsequently ignited after the assassination of the Liberal presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Eli%C3%A9cer_Gait%C3%A1n" title="Jorge Eliécer Gaitán">Jorge Eliécer Gaitán</a> on 9 April 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[97]</a></sup> The ensuing riots in Bogotá, known as <a href="/wiki/El_Bogotazo" class="mw-redirect" title="El Bogotazo">El Bogotazo</a>, spread throughout the country and claimed the lives of at least 180,000 Colombians.<sup id="cite_ref-Encarta_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-103">[98]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Colombia entered the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a> when <a href="/wiki/Laureano_G%C3%B3mez" title="Laureano Gómez">Laureano Gómez</a> was elected president. It was the only Latin American country to join the war in a direct military role as an ally of the United States. Particularly important was the resistance of the Colombian troops at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Old_Baldy" title="Battle of Old Baldy">Old Baldy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Colombia's_legacy_with_Korea_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombia's_legacy_with_Korea-104">[99]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The violence between the two political parties decreased first when <a href="/wiki/Gustavo_Rojas_Pinilla" title="Gustavo Rojas Pinilla">Gustavo Rojas</a> deposed the <a href="/wiki/Laureano_G%C3%B3mez" title="Laureano Gómez">President</a> of Colombia in a coup d'état and negotiated with the guerrillas, and then under the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Military_Junta" title="Colombian Military Junta">military junta</a> of General <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Par%C3%ADs" class="mw-redirect" title="Gabriel París">Gabriel París</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Centro_de_Memoria_Hist%C3%B3rica_-_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Centro_de_Memoria_Hist%C3%B3rica_-_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg/220px-Centro_de_Memoria_Hist%C3%B3rica_-_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Centro_de_Memoria_Hist%C3%B3rica_-_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg/330px-Centro_de_Memoria_Hist%C3%B3rica_-_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Centro_de_Memoria_Hist%C3%B3rica_-_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg/440px-Centro_de_Memoria_Hist%C3%B3rica_-_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4232" data-file-height="3134"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Centro_de_Memoria_Hist%C3%B3rica_-_Bogot%C3%A1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Axis of Peace and Memory, a memorial to the victims of the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_conflict" title="Colombian conflict">Colombian conflict</a> (1964–present)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After Rojas' deposition, the Colombian Conservative Party and Colombian Liberal Party agreed to create the <a href="/wiki/National_Front_(Colombia)" title="National Front (Colombia)">National Front</a>, a coalition that would jointly govern the country. Under the deal, the presidency would alternate between conservatives and liberals every 4 years for 16 years; the two parties would have parity in all other elective offices.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[102]</a></sup> The National Front ended "La Violencia", and National Front administrations attempted to institute far-reaching social and economic reforms in cooperation with the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_for_Progress" title="Alliance for Progress">Alliance for Progress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[104]</a></sup> Despite the progress in certain sectors, many social and political problems continued, and guerrilla groups were formally created such as the <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Armed_Forces_of_Colombia" title="Revolutionary Armed Forces of Colombia">FARC</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_Army_(Colombia)" title="National Liberation Army (Colombia)">ELN</a> and the <a href="/wiki/19th_of_April_Movement" title="19th of April Movement">M-19</a> to fight the government and political apparatus.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[105]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since the 1960s, the country has suffered from an <a href="/wiki/Asymmetric_warfare" title="Asymmetric warfare">asymmetric</a> <a href="/wiki/Low_intensity_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Low intensity conflict">low-intensity</a> <a href="/wiki/Colombian_armed_conflict_(1964%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="Colombian armed conflict (1964–present)">armed conflict</a> between <a href="/wiki/Military_Forces_of_Colombia" title="Military Forces of Colombia">government forces</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_movements_in_Colombia" title="Guerrilla movements in Colombia">leftist guerrilla groups</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paramilitarism_in_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Paramilitarism in Colombia">right wing paramilitaries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HistoricalCommission_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistoricalCommission-111">[106]</a></sup> The conflict escalated in the 1990s,<sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_armed_conflict_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_armed_conflict-112">[107]</a></sup> mainly in remote rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_conflict_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_conflict-113">[108]</a></sup> Since the beginning of the armed conflict, <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_defenders" class="mw-redirect" title="Human rights defenders">human rights defenders</a> have fought for the respect for human rights, despite staggering opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[Note 5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[Note 6]</a></sup> Several guerrillas' organizations decided to demobilize after peace negotiations in 1989–1994.<sup id="cite_ref-Enough_Already!_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Enough_Already!-15">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The United States has been heavily involved in the conflict since its beginnings, when in the early 1960s the <a href="/wiki/U.S._government" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. government">U.S. government</a> encouraged the Colombian military to attack leftist militias in rural Colombia. This was part of the U.S. fight against communism. <a href="/wiki/Mercenarie" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercenarie">Mercenaries</a> and multinational corporations such as <a href="/wiki/Chiquita_Brands_International" title="Chiquita Brands International">Chiquita Brands International</a> are some of the international actors that have contributed to the violence of the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-HistoricalCommission_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HistoricalCommission-111">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Enough_Already!_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Enough_Already!-15">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-colombia-and-us-54_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colombia-and-us-54-119">[112]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Beginning in the mid-1970s Colombian <a href="/wiki/Drug_cartel" title="Drug cartel">drug cartels</a> became major producers, processors and exporters of <a href="/wiki/Illegal_drug_trade_in_Colombia" title="Illegal drug trade in Colombia">illegal drugs</a>, primarily <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">marijuana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[113]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 4 July 1991, a new <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Constitution_of_1991" title="Colombian Constitution of 1991">Constitution</a> was promulgated. The changes generated by the new constitution are viewed as positive by Colombian society.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_Constitution_of_1991_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_Constitution_of_1991-122">[115]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Jefa_de_Estado_participa_en_ceremonia_de_la_Firma_de_la_Paz_entre_el_Gobierno_de_Colombia_y_las_FARC_E.P._(29953487045).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Jefa_de_Estado_participa_en_ceremonia_de_la_Firma_de_la_Paz_entre_el_Gobierno_de_Colombia_y_las_FARC_E.P._%2829953487045%29.jpg/230px-Jefa_de_Estado_participa_en_ceremonia_de_la_Firma_de_la_Paz_entre_el_Gobierno_de_Colombia_y_las_FARC_E.P._%2829953487045%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Jefa_de_Estado_participa_en_ceremonia_de_la_Firma_de_la_Paz_entre_el_Gobierno_de_Colombia_y_las_FARC_E.P._%2829953487045%29.jpg/345px-Jefa_de_Estado_participa_en_ceremonia_de_la_Firma_de_la_Paz_entre_el_Gobierno_de_Colombia_y_las_FARC_E.P._%2829953487045%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Jefa_de_Estado_participa_en_ceremonia_de_la_Firma_de_la_Paz_entre_el_Gobierno_de_Colombia_y_las_FARC_E.P._%2829953487045%29.jpg/460px-Jefa_de_Estado_participa_en_ceremonia_de_la_Firma_de_la_Paz_entre_el_Gobierno_de_Colombia_y_las_FARC_E.P._%2829953487045%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3307" data-file-height="2206"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Jefa_de_Estado_participa_en_ceremonia_de_la_Firma_de_la_Paz_entre_el_Gobierno_de_Colombia_y_las_FARC_E.P._(29953487045).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Former President <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Santos" title="Juan Manuel Santos">Juan Manuel Santos</a> signed a <a href="/wiki/Colombian_peace_process" title="Colombian peace process">peace accord</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The administration of President <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_Uribe" title="Álvaro Uribe">Álvaro Uribe</a> (2002–10), adopted the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_security_policy" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic security policy">democratic security policy</a> which included an integrated <a href="/wiki/Counter-terrorism" title="Counter-terrorism">counter-terrorism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Counter-insurgency" class="mw-redirect" title="Counter-insurgency">counter-insurgency</a> campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[116]</a></sup> The Government economic plan also promoted confidence in investors.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[117]</a></sup> As part of a controversial peace process the <a href="/wiki/United_Self-Defense_Forces_of_Colombia" title="United Self-Defense Forces of Colombia">AUC</a> (right-wing paramilitaries) as a formal organization had ceased to function.<sup id="cite_ref-CIAWFB_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIAWFB-125">[118]</a></sup> In February 2008, millions of Colombians demonstrated against FARC and other outlawed groups.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[119]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After peace negotiations in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Colombia" title="Government of Colombia">Colombian government</a> of President <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Santos" title="Juan Manuel Santos">Juan Manuel Santos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Guerrilla">guerrilla</a> of FARC-EP announced a final agreement to end the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[120]</a></sup> However, a <a href="/wiki/Colombian_peace_agreement_referendum,_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="Colombian peace agreement referendum, 2016">referendum</a> to ratify the deal was unsuccessful.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[122]</a></sup> Afterward, the Colombian government and the FARC signed a revised <a href="/wiki/Colombian_peace_process" title="Colombian peace process">peace deal</a> in November 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[123]</a></sup> which the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_congress" class="mw-redirect" title="Colombian congress">Colombian congress</a> approved.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[124]</a></sup> In 2016, President Santos was awarded the <a href="/wiki/2016_Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="2016 Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[125]</a></sup> The Government began a process of attention and comprehensive reparation for victims of conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[127]</a></sup> Colombia shows modest progress in the struggle to defend human rights, as expressed by <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">HRW</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[128]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Special_Jurisdiction_of_Peace" title="Special Jurisdiction of Peace">Special Jurisdiction of Peace</a> has been created to investigate, clarify, prosecute and punish serious human rights violations and grave breaches of <a href="/wiki/International_humanitarian_law" title="International humanitarian law">international humanitarian law</a> which occurred during the armed conflict and to satisfy victims' right to <a href="/wiki/Justice" title="Justice">justice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[129]</a></sup> During his visit to Colombia, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a> paid tribute to the victims of the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In June 2018, <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Duque" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivan Duque">Ivan Duque</a>, the candidate of the right-wing <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Center_(Colombia)" title="Democratic Center (Colombia)">Democratic Centre</a> party, won the presidential <a href="/wiki/2018_Colombian_presidential_election" title="2018 Colombian presidential election">election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[131]</a></sup> On 7 August 2018, he was sworn in as the new President of Colombia.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[132]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/2010_Colombia%E2%80%93Venezuela_diplomatic_crisis" title="2010 Colombia–Venezuela diplomatic crisis">Colombia's relations with Venezuela</a> have fluctuated due to ideological differences between both governments.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[133]</a></sup> Colombia has offered <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_aid" title="Humanitarian aid">humanitarian support</a> with food and medicines to mitigate the shortage of supplies in Venezuela.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[134]</a></sup> Colombia's Foreign Ministry said that all efforts to resolve <a href="/wiki/Crisis_in_Venezuela_(2012%E2%80%93present)" class="mw-redirect" title="Crisis in Venezuela (2012–present)">Venezuela's crisis</a> should be peaceful.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[135]</a></sup> Colombia proposed the idea of the <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a> and a final document was adopted by the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[136]</a></sup> In February 2019, Venezuelan president <a href="/wiki/Nicol%C3%A1s_Maduro" title="Nicolás Maduro">Nicolás Maduro</a> cut off diplomatic relations with Colombia after Colombian President Ivan Duque had helped Venezuelan opposition politicians deliver humanitarian aid to their country. Colombia recognized Venezuelan opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Juan_Guaid%C3%B3" title="Juan Guaidó">Juan Guaidó</a> as the country's legitimate president. In January 2020, Colombia rejected Maduro's proposal that the two countries would restore diplomatic relations.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[137]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Colombia" title="Geography of Colombia">Geography of Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Colombia" title="Geology of Colombia">Geology of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Colombia" title="List of national parks of Colombia">List of national parks of Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_in_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="List of rivers in Colombia">List of rivers in Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mapa_de_Colombia_(relieve).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Mapa_de_Colombia_%28relieve%29.svg/230px-Mapa_de_Colombia_%28relieve%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="230" height="260" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Mapa_de_Colombia_%28relieve%29.svg/345px-Mapa_de_Colombia_%28relieve%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Mapa_de_Colombia_%28relieve%29.svg/460px-Mapa_de_Colombia_%28relieve%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2072" data-file-height="2339"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mapa_de_Colombia_(relieve).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Relief map
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The geography of Colombia is characterized by its six main <a href="/wiki/Natural_regions_of_Colombia" title="Natural regions of Colombia">natural regions</a> that present their own unique characteristics, from the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> mountain range region shared with Ecuador and Venezuela; the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Coast">Pacific Coastal</a> region shared with Panama and Ecuador; the Caribbean coastal region shared with Venezuela and Panama; the <i><a href="/wiki/Llanos" title="Llanos">Llanos</a></i> (plains) shared with Venezuela; the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Rainforest" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Rainforest">Amazon Rainforest</a> region shared with Venezuela, Brazil, Peru and Ecuador; to the <a href="/wiki/Insular_Region_(Colombia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Insular Region (Colombia)">insular area</a>, comprising islands in both the Atlantic and Pacific oceans.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_of_Colombia_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography_of_Colombia-145">[138]</a></sup> It shares its maritime limits with <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Maritime_borders_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maritime_borders-146">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Colombia is bordered to the northwest by <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>, to the east by <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> and Brazil, and to the south by <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-Land_borders_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Land_borders-147">[140]</a></sup> it established its maritime boundaries with neighboring countries through seven agreements on the Caribbean Sea and three on the Pacific Ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-Maritime_borders_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maritime_borders-146">[139]</a></sup> It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/12th_parallel_north" title="12th parallel north">12°N</a> and <a href="/wiki/4th_parallel_south" title="4th parallel south">4°S</a> and between longitudes <a href="/wiki/67th_meridian_west" title="67th meridian west">67°</a> and <a href="/wiki/79th_meridian_west" title="79th meridian west">79°W</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_COL_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Koppen-Geiger_Map_COL_present.svg/290px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_COL_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Koppen-Geiger_Map_COL_present.svg/435px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_COL_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Koppen-Geiger_Map_COL_present.svg/580px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_COL_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1263" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_COL_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Colombia map of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Part of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ring_of_Fire" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Ring of Fire">Ring of Fire</a>, a region of the world subject to earthquakes and <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanic eruptions</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ring_of_Fire_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ring_of_Fire-148">[141]</a></sup> in the interior of Colombia the Andes are the prevailing geographical feature. Most of Colombia's population centers are located in these interior highlands. Beyond the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Massif" title="Colombian Massif">Colombian Massif</a> (in the southwestern departments of <a href="/wiki/Cauca_Department" title="Cauca Department">Cauca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nari%C3%B1o_Department" title="Nariño Department">Nariño</a>), these are divided into three branches known as <i>cordilleras</i> (mountain ranges): the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Occidental_(Colombia)" title="Cordillera Occidental (Colombia)">Cordillera Occidental</a>, running adjacent to the Pacific coast and including the city of <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Cali" class="mw-redirect" title="Santiago de Cali">Cali</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Colombia)" title="Cordillera Central (Colombia)">Cordillera Central</a>, running between the <a href="/wiki/Cauca_River" title="Cauca River">Cauca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_River" title="Magdalena River">Magdalena River</a> valleys (to the west and east, respectively) and including the cities of <a href="/wiki/Medell%C3%ADn" title="Medellín">Medellín</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manizales" title="Manizales">Manizales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pereira,_Colombia" title="Pereira, Colombia">Pereira</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Armenia,_Quind%C3%ADo" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenia, Quindío">Armenia</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Oriental_(Colombia)" title="Cordillera Oriental (Colombia)">Cordillera Oriental</a>, extending northeast to the <a href="/wiki/Guajira_Peninsula" title="Guajira Peninsula">Guajira Peninsula</a> and including Bogotá, <a href="/wiki/Bucaramanga" title="Bucaramanga">Bucaramanga</a>, and <a href="/wiki/C%C3%BAcuta" title="Cúcuta">Cúcuta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_of_Colombia_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography_of_Colombia-145">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-populationbyregions_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-populationbyregions-149">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Population_density_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population_density-150">[143]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Peaks in the Cordillera Occidental exceed 4,700&nbsp;m (15,420&nbsp;ft), and in the Cordillera Central and Cordillera Oriental they reach 5,000&nbsp;m (16,404&nbsp;ft). At 2,600&nbsp;m (8,530&nbsp;ft), Bogotá is the highest city of its size in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_of_Colombia_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography_of_Colombia-145">[138]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>East of the Andes lies the <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Llanos" title="Llanos">Llanos</a></i>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Orinoco" title="Orinoco">Orinoco</a> River basin, and in the far southeast, the <a href="/wiki/Jungle" title="Jungle">jungle</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon rainforest</a>. Together these lowlands make up over half Colombia's territory, but they contain less than 6% of the population. To the north the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Region_of_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean Region of Colombia">Caribbean coast</a>, home to 21.9% of the population and the location of the major port cities of <a href="/wiki/Barranquilla" title="Barranquilla">Barranquilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Colombia" title="Cartagena, Colombia">Cartagena</a>, generally consists of low-lying plains, but it also contains the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_de_Santa_Marta" title="Sierra Nevada de Santa Marta">Sierra Nevada de Santa Marta</a> mountain range, which includes the country's tallest peaks (<a href="/wiki/Pico_Crist%C3%B3bal_Col%C3%B3n" title="Pico Cristóbal Colón">Pico Cristóbal Colón</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pico_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Pico Simón Bolívar">Pico Simón Bolívar</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/La_Guajira_Desert" title="La Guajira Desert">La Guajira Desert</a>. By contrast the narrow and discontinuous <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Region_of_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Region of Colombia">Pacific coastal lowlands</a>, backed by the <a href="/wiki/Baud%C3%B3_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Baudó Mountains">Serranía de Baudó</a> mountains, are sparsely populated and covered in dense vegetation. The principal Pacific port is <a href="/wiki/Buenaventura,_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Buenaventura, Colombia">Buenaventura</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_of_Colombia_145-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography_of_Colombia-145">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-populationbyregions_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-populationbyregions-149">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Population_density_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population_density-150">[143]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The main rivers of Colombia are <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_River" title="Magdalena River">Magdalena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cauca_River" title="Cauca River">Cauca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guaviare_River" title="Guaviare River">Guaviare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atrato_River" title="Atrato River">Atrato</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meta_River" title="Meta River">Meta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Putumayo_River" title="Putumayo River">Putumayo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caquet%C3%A1_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Caquetá River">Caquetá</a>. Colombia has four main drainage systems: the Pacific drain, the Caribbean drain, the Orinoco Basin and the Amazon Basin. The <a href="/wiki/Orinoco" title="Orinoco">Orinoco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon</a> Rivers mark limits with Colombia to Venezuela and Peru respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Hydrography_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hydrography-151">[144]</a></sup> </p>
