      <p>Protected areas and the "National Park System" cover an area of about 14,268,224 hectares (142,682.24&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) and account for 12.77% of the Colombian territory.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[145]</a></sup> Compared to neighboring countries, rates of <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Colombia" title="Deforestation in Colombia">deforestation in Colombia</a> are still relatively low.<sup id="cite_ref-United_Nations_Deforestation_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_Nations_Deforestation-153">[146]</a></sup> Colombia had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 8.26/10, ranking it 25th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-154">[147]</a></sup> Colombia is the sixth country in the world by magnitude of total renewable freshwater supply, and still has large reserves of freshwater.<sup id="cite_ref-worldwater_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldwater-155">[148]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Colombia" title="Climate of Colombia">Climate of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nevado_del_tolima_y_sus_frailejones.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Nevado_del_tolima_y_sus_frailejones.jpg/220px-Nevado_del_tolima_y_sus_frailejones.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Nevado_del_tolima_y_sus_frailejones.jpg/330px-Nevado_del_tolima_y_sus_frailejones.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Nevado_del_tolima_y_sus_frailejones.jpg/440px-Nevado_del_tolima_y_sus_frailejones.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nevado_del_tolima_y_sus_frailejones.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mountain climate is one of the unique features of the Andes and other high altitude reliefs
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The climate of Colombia is characterized for being tropical presenting variations within <a href="/wiki/Natural_regions_of_Colombia" title="Natural regions of Colombia">six natural regions</a> and depending on the altitude, temperature, <a href="/wiki/Humidity" title="Humidity">humidity</a>, winds and rainfall.<sup id="cite_ref-Thermal_floors_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thermal_floors-156">[149]</a></sup> The diversity of climate zones in Colombia is characterized for having <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest" title="Tropical rainforest">tropical rainforests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savannas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">deserts</a> and mountain climate. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Mountain_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountain climate">Mountain climate</a> is one of the unique features of the Andes and other high altitude reliefs where climate is determined by elevation. Below 1,000 meters (3,281&nbsp;ft) in elevation is the <a href="/wiki/Tierra_caliente" title="Tierra caliente">warm altitudinal zone</a>, where temperatures are above 24&nbsp;°C (75.2&nbsp;°F). About 82.5% of the country's total area lies in the warm altitudinal zone. The <a href="/wiki/Tierra_templada" title="Tierra templada">temperate climate altitudinal zone</a> located between 1,001 and 2,000 meters (3,284 and 6,562&nbsp;ft) is characterized for presenting an average temperature ranging between 17 and 24&nbsp;°C (62.6 and 75.2&nbsp;°F). The <a href="/wiki/Tierra_fr%C3%ADa" title="Tierra fría">cold climate</a> is present between 2,001 and 3,000 meters (6,565 and 9,843&nbsp;ft) and the temperatures vary between 12 and 17&nbsp;°C (53.6 and 62.6&nbsp;°F). Beyond lies the alpine conditions of the forested zone and then the treeless grasslands of the <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A1ramo" title="Páramo">páramos</a>. Above 4,000 meters (13,123&nbsp;ft), where temperatures are below freezing, the climate is <a href="/wiki/Tierra_helada" title="Tierra helada">glacial</a>, a zone of permanent snow and ice.<sup id="cite_ref-Thermal_floors_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thermal_floors-156">[149]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_of_Colombia" title="Biodiversity of Colombia">Biodiversity of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_Colombia" title="Fauna of Colombia">Fauna of Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flora_of_Colombia" title="Flora of Colombia">Flora of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cattleya_trianae_tipo_Baronessa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Cattleya_trianae_tipo_Baronessa.jpg/220px-Cattleya_trianae_tipo_Baronessa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Cattleya_trianae_tipo_Baronessa.jpg/330px-Cattleya_trianae_tipo_Baronessa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Cattleya_trianae_tipo_Baronessa.jpg/440px-Cattleya_trianae_tipo_Baronessa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3200" data-file-height="2400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cattleya_trianae_tipo_Baronessa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The national flower of Colombia, the <a href="/wiki/Endemic" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic">endemic</a> <a href="/wiki/Orchid" class="mw-redirect" title="Orchid">orchid</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Cattleya_trianae" title="Cattleya trianae">Cattleya trianae</a></i>, is named for Colombian botanist and physician <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Jer%C3%B3nimo_Triana" title="José Jerónimo Triana">José Jerónimo Triana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[150]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Colombia is one of the <a href="/wiki/Megadiverse_countries" title="Megadiverse countries">megadiverse countries</a> in <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[151]</a></sup> ranking first in <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Colombia" title="List of birds of Colombia">bird species</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bird_Species_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bird_Species-159">[152]</a></sup> As for plants, the country has between 40,000 and 45,000 plant <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a>, equivalent to 10 or 20% of total global species, which is even more remarkable given that Colombia is considered a country of intermediate size.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[153]</a></sup> Colombia is the second most biodiverse country in the world, lagging only after Brazil which is approximately 7 times bigger.<sup id="cite_ref-Biodiversity_of_Colombia_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Biodiversity_of_Colombia-17">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Colombia is the country with the planet's highest biodiversity, having the highest rate of species by area as well as the largest number of <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemisms</a> (species that are not found naturally anywhere else) of any country. About 10% of the species of the Earth live in Colombia, including over 1,900 species of bird, more than in Europe and North America combined. Colombia has 10% of the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Colombia" title="List of mammals of Colombia">mammals</a> species, 14% of the <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">amphibian</a> species and 18% of the <a href="/wiki/Endemic_birds_of_Colombia" title="Endemic birds of Colombia">bird</a> species of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-DIVERSITY_OF_SPECIES_IN_COLOMBIA_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DIVERSITY_OF_SPECIES_IN_COLOMBIA-161">[154]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Colombia has about 2,000 species of <a href="/wiki/Marine_fish" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine fish">marine fish</a> and is the second most diverse country in <a href="/wiki/Freshwater_fish" title="Freshwater fish">freshwater fish</a>. It is also the country with the most endemic species of <a href="/wiki/List_of_butterflies_of_Colombia" title="List of butterflies of Colombia">butterflies</a>, is first in <a href="/wiki/Orchid" class="mw-redirect" title="Orchid">orchid</a> species, and has approximately 7,000 species of <a href="/wiki/Beetle" title="Beetle">beetles</a>. Colombia is second in the number of amphibian species and is the third most diverse country in <a href="/wiki/List_of_reptiles_of_Colombia" title="List of reptiles of Colombia">reptiles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arecaceae" title="Arecaceae">palms</a>. There are about 1,900 species of <a href="/wiki/Mollusk" class="mw-redirect" title="Mollusk">mollusks</a> and according to estimates there are about 300,000 species of <a href="/wiki/Invertebrates" class="mw-redirect" title="Invertebrates">invertebrates</a> in the country. In Colombia there are 32 terrestrial <a href="/wiki/Biomes" class="mw-redirect" title="Biomes">biomes</a> and 314 types of <a href="/wiki/Ecosystems" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecosystems">ecosystems</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-humboldt_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-humboldt-163">[156]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Colombia" title="Government of Colombia">Government of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Constitution_of_1991" title="Colombian Constitution of 1991">Colombian Constitution of 1991</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lado_sur_Casa_de_Nari%C3%B1o.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Lado_sur_Casa_de_Nari%C3%B1o.jpg/250px-Lado_sur_Casa_de_Nari%C3%B1o.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Lado_sur_Casa_de_Nari%C3%B1o.jpg/375px-Lado_sur_Casa_de_Nari%C3%B1o.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Lado_sur_Casa_de_Nari%C3%B1o.jpg/500px-Lado_sur_Casa_de_Nari%C3%B1o.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="539"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lado_sur_Casa_de_Nari%C3%B1o.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Casa_de_Nari%C3%B1o" title="Casa de Nariño">Casa de Nariño</a> is the official home and principal workplace of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Colombia" title="President of Colombia">President of Colombia</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The government of Colombia takes place within the framework of a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Participatory_democracy" title="Participatory democracy">participatory democratic</a> republic as established in the Constitution of 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_Constitution_of_1991_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_Constitution_of_1991-122">[115]</a></sup> In accordance with the principle of <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">separation of powers</a>, government is divided into three branches: the executive branch, the legislative branch and the judicial branch.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[157]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As the head of the executive branch, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Colombia" title="President of Colombia">President of Colombia</a> serves as both <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_Colombia" title="Vice President of Colombia">Vice President</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_the_Republic_of_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Ministers of the Republic of Colombia">Council of Ministers</a>. The president is elected by popular vote to serve a single four-year term (In 2015, Colombia's Congress approved the repeal of a 2004 constitutional amendment that changed the one-term limit for presidents to a two-term limit).<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[158]</a></sup> At the provincial level executive power is vested in <a href="/wiki/List_of_Colombian_Department_Governors" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Colombian Department Governors">department governors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Colombia" title="Municipalities of Colombia">municipal mayors</a> and local administrators for smaller administrative subdivisions, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Corregimientos_of_Colombia" title="Corregimientos of Colombia">corregimientos</a></i> or <i>comunas</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[159]</a></sup> All regional elections are held one year and five months after the presidential election.<sup id="cite_ref-Government_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Government-167">[160]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[161]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:El_Capitolio_Nacional_(Bogot%C3%A1,_Colombia)_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/El_Capitolio_Nacional_%28Bogot%C3%A1%2C_Colombia%29_1.jpg/250px-El_Capitolio_Nacional_%28Bogot%C3%A1%2C_Colombia%29_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/El_Capitolio_Nacional_%28Bogot%C3%A1%2C_Colombia%29_1.jpg/375px-El_Capitolio_Nacional_%28Bogot%C3%A1%2C_Colombia%29_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/El_Capitolio_Nacional_%28Bogot%C3%A1%2C_Colombia%29_1.jpg/500px-El_Capitolio_Nacional_%28Bogot%C3%A1%2C_Colombia%29_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1832"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:El_Capitolio_Nacional_(Bogot%C3%A1,_Colombia)_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Capitolio_Nacional" title="Capitolio Nacional">Capitolio Nacional</a> seat of the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Colombia" title="Congress of Colombia">Congress</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The legislative branch of government is represented nationally by the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Colombia" title="Congress of Colombia">Congress</a>, a bicameral institution comprising a 166-seat <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Representatives_of_Colombia" title="Chamber of Representatives of Colombia">Chamber of Representatives</a> and a 102-seat <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Colombia" title="Senate of Colombia">Senate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[163]</a></sup> The Senate is elected nationally and the Chamber of Representatives is elected in electoral districts.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[164]</a></sup> Members of both houses are elected to serve four-year terms two months before the president, also by popular vote.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[165]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The judicial branch is headed by <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Colombia" title="Judiciary of Colombia">four high courts</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[166]</a></sup> consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Justice_of_Colombia" title="Supreme Court of Justice of Colombia">Supreme Court</a> which deals with penal and civil matters, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_State_of_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of State of Colombia">Council of State</a>, which has special responsibility for <a href="/wiki/Administrative_law" title="Administrative law">administrative law</a> and also provides legal advice to the executive, the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Colombia" title="Constitutional Court of Colombia">Constitutional Court</a>, responsible for assuring the integrity of the Colombian constitution, and the <a href="/wiki/Superior_Council_of_Judicature" title="Superior Council of Judicature">Superior Council of Judicature</a>, responsible for auditing the judicial branch.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[167]</a></sup> Colombia operates a system of <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a>, which since 2005 has been applied through an <a href="/wiki/Adversarial_system" title="Adversarial system">adversarial system</a>. </p>
      <p>Despite a number of controversies, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_security_policy" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic security policy">democratic security policy</a> has ensured that former President <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_Uribe" title="Álvaro Uribe">Uribe</a> remained popular among Colombian people, with his approval rating peaking at 76%, according to a poll in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[168]</a></sup> However, having served two terms, he was constitutionally barred from seeking re-election in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[169]</a></sup> In the run-off elections on 20 June 2010 the former Minister of defense <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Santos" title="Juan Manuel Santos">Juan Manuel Santos</a> won with 69% of the vote against the second most popular candidate, <a href="/wiki/Antanas_Mockus" title="Antanas Mockus">Antanas Mockus</a>. A second round was required since no candidate received over the 50% winning threshold of votes.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[170]</a></sup> Santos won nearly 51% of the vote in second-round elections on 15 June 2014, beating right-wing rival <a href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_Iv%C3%A1n_Zuluaga" title="Óscar Iván Zuluaga">Óscar Iván Zuluaga</a>, who won 45%.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[171]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Iv%C3%A1n_Duque" class="mw-redirect" title="Iván Duque">Iván Duque</a> won in the second round with 54% of the vote, against 42% for his left-wing rival, <a href="/wiki/Gustavo_Petro" title="Gustavo Petro">Gustavo Petro</a>. His term as Colombia's president runs for four years beginning 7 August 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[172]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_affairs">Foreign affairs</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Colombia" title="Foreign relations of Colombia">Foreign relations of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_missions_of_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Diplomatic missions of Colombia">Diplomatic missions of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:VII_Cumbre_de_la_Alianza_del_Pac%C3%ADfico,_Santiago_de_Cali.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/VII_Cumbre_de_la_Alianza_del_Pac%C3%ADfico%2C_Santiago_de_Cali.jpg/220px-VII_Cumbre_de_la_Alianza_del_Pac%C3%ADfico%2C_Santiago_de_Cali.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/VII_Cumbre_de_la_Alianza_del_Pac%C3%ADfico%2C_Santiago_de_Cali.jpg/330px-VII_Cumbre_de_la_Alianza_del_Pac%C3%ADfico%2C_Santiago_de_Cali.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/VII_Cumbre_de_la_Alianza_del_Pac%C3%ADfico%2C_Santiago_de_Cali.jpg/440px-VII_Cumbre_de_la_Alianza_del_Pac%C3%ADfico%2C_Santiago_de_Cali.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2031" data-file-height="1214"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:VII_Cumbre_de_la_Alianza_del_Pac%C3%ADfico,_Santiago_de_Cali.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The VII Summit of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Alliance" title="Pacific Alliance">Pacific Alliance</a>: Former President of Colombia, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Santos" title="Juan Manuel Santos">Juan Manuel Santos</a> is second from the left.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The foreign affairs of Colombia are headed by the President, as head of state, and managed by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Colombia)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Colombia)">Minister of Foreign Affairs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_foreign_affairs_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_foreign_affairs-180">[173]</a></sup> Colombia has diplomatic missions in all continents.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[174]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Colombia was one of the 4 founding members of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Alliance" title="Pacific Alliance">Pacific Alliance</a>, which is a political, economic and co-operative integration mechanism that promotes the free circulation of goods, services, capital and persons between the members, as well as a common stock exchange and joint embassies in several countries.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Pacific_Alliance_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Pacific_Alliance-182">[175]</a></sup> Colombia is also a member of the United Nations, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Ibero-American_States" title="Organization of Ibero-American States">Organization of Ibero-American States</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Andean_Community_of_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Andean Community of Nations">Andean Community of Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[177]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[178]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[180]</a></sup> Colombia is a global partner of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[181]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Colombia">Military of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Colombian_Air_Force_Sikorsky_UH-60L_Arp%C3%ADa_III_(S-70A-41)_Ram%C3%ADrez-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Colombian_Air_Force_Sikorsky_UH-60L_Arp%C3%ADa_III_%28S-70A-41%29_Ram%C3%ADrez-1.jpg/220px-Colombian_Air_Force_Sikorsky_UH-60L_Arp%C3%ADa_III_%28S-70A-41%29_Ram%C3%ADrez-1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Colombian_Air_Force_Sikorsky_UH-60L_Arp%C3%ADa_III_%28S-70A-41%29_Ram%C3%ADrez-1.jpg/330px-Colombian_Air_Force_Sikorsky_UH-60L_Arp%C3%ADa_III_%28S-70A-41%29_Ram%C3%ADrez-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Colombian_Air_Force_Sikorsky_UH-60L_Arp%C3%ADa_III_%28S-70A-41%29_Ram%C3%ADrez-1.jpg/440px-Colombian_Air_Force_Sikorsky_UH-60L_Arp%C3%ADa_III_%28S-70A-41%29_Ram%C3%ADrez-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Colombian_Air_Force_Sikorsky_UH-60L_Arp%C3%ADa_III_(S-70A-41)_Ram%C3%ADrez-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Sikorsky_UH-60_Black_Hawk" title="Sikorsky UH-60 Black Hawk">Arpía III</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Air_Force" title="Colombian Air Force">Colombian Air Force</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The executive branch of government is responsible for managing the defense of Colombia, with the President <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the armed forces. The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Defence_(Colombia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of National Defence (Colombia)">Ministry of Defence</a> exercises day-to-day control of the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Colombia">military</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_National_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="Colombian National Police">Colombian National Police</a>. Colombia has 455,461 active military personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[182]</a></sup> And in 2016 3.4% of the country's GDP went towards military expenditure, placing it 24th in the world. Colombia's armed forces are the largest in Latin America, and it is the second largest spender on its military after Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[184]</a></sup> In 2018, Colombia signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[185]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Colombian military is divided into three branches: the <a href="/wiki/National_Army_of_Colombia" title="National Army of Colombia">National Army of Colombia</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Air_Force" title="Colombian Air Force">Colombian Air Force</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Navy" title="Colombian Navy">Colombian Navy</a>. The National Police functions as a <a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">gendarmerie</a>, operating independently from the military as the law enforcement agency for the entire country. Each of these operates with their own intelligence apparatus separate from the <a href="/wiki/National_Intelligence_Directorate_(Colombia)" title="National Intelligence Directorate (Colombia)">National Intelligence Directorate</a> (DNI, in Spanish).<sup id="cite_ref-The_Colombian_military_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Colombian_military-193">[186]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The National Army is formed by divisions, brigades, special brigades, and special units,<sup id="cite_ref-The_National_Army_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_National_Army-194">[187]</a></sup> the Colombian Navy by the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Naval_Infantry" title="Colombian Naval Infantry">Naval Infantry</a>, the Naval Force of the Caribbean, the Naval Force of the Pacific, the Naval Force of the South, the Naval Force of the East, Colombia Coast Guards, Naval Aviation, and the Specific Command of San Andres y Providencia<sup id="cite_ref-the_National_Armada_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the_National_Armada-195">[188]</a></sup> and the Air Force by 15 air units.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Air_Force_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Air_Force-196">[189]</a></sup> The National Police has a presence in all municipalities. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Colombia" title="Departments of Colombia">Departments of Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Colombia" title="Municipalities of Colombia">Municipalities of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities in Colombia">List of cities in Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corregimientos_of_Colombia" title="Corregimientos of Colombia">Corregimientos of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Colombia is divided into 32 <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Colombia" title="Departments of Colombia">departments</a> and one <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogotá">capital district</a>, which is treated as a department (Bogotá also serves as the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Cundinamarca_Department" title="Cundinamarca Department">department of Cundinamarca</a>). Departments are subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Colombia" title="Municipalities of Colombia">municipalities</a>, each of which is assigned a municipal seat, and municipalities are in turn subdivided into <i><a href="/wiki/Corregimientos_of_Colombia" title="Corregimientos of Colombia">corregimientos</a></i> in rural areas and into <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comunas_of_Colombia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Comunas of Colombia (page does not exist)">comunas</a></i> in urban areas. Each department has a local government with a governor and assembly directly elected to four-year terms, and each municipality is headed by a mayor and council. There is a popularly elected local administrative board in each of the <i>corregimientos</i> or <i>comunas</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Administrative_divisions_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Administrative_divisions-197">[190]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Concerning_the_territorial_organization_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Concerning_the_territorial_organization-198">[191]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[193]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In addition to the capital four other cities have been designated <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Colombia" title="Districts of Colombia">districts</a> (in effect special municipalities), on the basis of special distinguishing features. These are <a href="/wiki/Barranquilla" title="Barranquilla">Barranquilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Colombia" title="Cartagena, Colombia">Cartagena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Marta" title="Santa Marta">Santa Marta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buenaventura,_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Buenaventura, Colombia">Buenaventura</a>. Some departments have local administrative subdivisions, where towns have a large concentration of population and municipalities are near each other (for example, in Antioquia and Cundinamarca). Where departments have a low population (for example Amazonas, Vaupés and Vichada), special administrative divisions are employed, such as "department <i>corregimientos</i>", which are a hybrid of a municipality and a <i>corregimiento</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Administrative_divisions_197-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Administrative_divisions-197">[190]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Concerning_the_territorial_organization_198-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Concerning_the_territorial_organization-198">[191]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><small>Click on a department on the map below to go to its article.</small> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities_and_towns">Largest cities and towns</span></h3> 
      <p>Colombia is a highly urbanized country with 77.1% of the population living in urban areas. The largest cities in the country are <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogotá">Bogotá</a>, with 7,387,400 inhabitants, <a href="/wiki/Medell%C3%ADn" title="Medellín">Medellín</a>, with 2,382,399 inhabitants, <a href="/wiki/Cali" title="Cali">Cali</a>, with 2,172,527 inhabitants, and <a href="/wiki/Barranquilla" title="Barranquilla">Barranquilla</a>, with 1,205,284 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[194]</a></sup> </p>

         <td rowspan="11" style="text-align: center"><a href="/wiki/File:Santiago_de_Cali.jpg" class="image" title="Cali"><img alt="Cali" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Santiago_de_Cali.jpg/120px-Santiago_de_Cali.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="80" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Santiago_de_Cali.jpg/180px-Santiago_de_Cali.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Santiago_de_Cali.jpg/240px-Santiago_de_Cali.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a><br><a href="/wiki/Cali" title="Cali">Cali</a><br><a href="/wiki/File:Barranquilla,_Colombia.jpg" class="image" title="Barranquilla"><img alt="Barranquilla" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Barranquilla%2C_Colombia.jpg/120px-Barranquilla%2C_Colombia.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="90" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Barranquilla%2C_Colombia.jpg/180px-Barranquilla%2C_Colombia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Barranquilla%2C_Colombia.jpg/240px-Barranquilla%2C_Colombia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112"></a><br><a href="/wiki/Barranquilla" title="Barranquilla">Barranquilla</a> </td>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Colombia" title="Economy of Colombia">Economy of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Colombia" title="Agriculture in Colombia">Agriculture in Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Industry_of_Colombia" title="Industry of Colombia">Industry of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Colombia_GDP_by_sector_in_2017.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Colombia_GDP_by_sector_in_2017.png/400px-Colombia_GDP_by_sector_in_2017.png" decoding="async" width="400" height="280" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Colombia_GDP_by_sector_in_2017.png/600px-Colombia_GDP_by_sector_in_2017.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e2/Colombia_GDP_by_sector_in_2017.png 2x" data-file-width="635" data-file-height="444"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Colombia_GDP_by_sector_in_2017.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Colombia GDP by sector in 2017.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Historically an agrarian economy, Colombia urbanised rapidly in the 20th century, by the end of which just 15.8% of the workforce were employed in agriculture, generating just 6.6% of GDP; 19.6% of the workforce were employed in industry and 64.6% in services, responsible for 33.4% and 59.9% of GDP respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-GDP_Composition_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GDP_Composition-203">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[197]</a></sup> The country's <a href="/wiki/Economic_production" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic production">economic production</a> is dominated by its strong <a href="/wiki/Domestic_demand" class="mw-redirect" title="Domestic demand">domestic demand</a>. <a href="/wiki/Consumer_spending" title="Consumer spending">Consumption expenditure</a> by households is the largest component of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-GDPCOLOMBIA_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GDPCOLOMBIA-205">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GDP_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GDP-18">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Colombianeconomy_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombianeconomy-206">[199]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Colombia's <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a> grew steadily in the latter part of the 20th century, with gross domestic product (GDP) increasing at an average rate of over 4% per year between 1970 and 1998. The country suffered a <a href="/wiki/Recession" title="Recession">recession</a> in 1999 (the first full year of negative growth since the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>), and the recovery from that recession was long and painful. However, in recent years growth has been impressive, reaching 6.9% in 2007, one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(real)_growth_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by GDP (real) growth rate">highest rates of growth</a> in Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-Colombia's_GDP_growth_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombia's_GDP_growth-16">[14]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> estimates, in 2012, Colombia's GDP (PPP) was US$500&nbsp;billion (<a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">28th in the world</a> and third in South America). </p>
      <p>Total <a href="/wiki/Government_expenditures" class="mw-redirect" title="Government expenditures">government expenditures</a> account for 27.9 percent of the domestic economy. <a href="/wiki/External_debt" title="External debt">External debt</a> equals 39.9 percent of gross domestic product. A strong fiscal climate was reaffirmed by a boost in <a href="/wiki/Bond_ratings" class="mw-redirect" title="Bond ratings">bond ratings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[200]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[201]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-heritage_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heritage-209">[202]</a></sup> Annual inflation closed 2017 at 4.09% YoY (vs. 5.75% YoY in 2016).<sup id="cite_ref-Inflation_Rate_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inflation_Rate-210">[203]</a></sup> The average national <a href="/wiki/Unemployment_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Unemployment rate">unemployment rate</a> in 2017 was 9.4%,<sup id="cite_ref-Unemployment_Rate_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unemployment_Rate-211">[204]</a></sup> although the informality is the biggest problem facing the <a href="/wiki/Labour_market" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour market">labour market</a> (the income of formal workers climbed 24.8% in 5 years while labor incomes of informal workers rose only 9%).<sup id="cite_ref-informal_workers_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-informal_workers-212">[205]</a></sup> Colombia has <a href="/wiki/Free-trade_zone" title="Free-trade zone">free-trade zone</a> (FTZ),<sup id="cite_ref-FTZ_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FTZ-213">[206]</a></sup> such as Zona Franca del Pacifico, located in the Valle del Cauca, one of the most striking areas for foreign investment.<sup id="cite_ref-Zonas_Francas_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zonas_Francas-214">[207]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Financial_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial sector">financial sector</a> has grown favorably due to good liquidity in the economy, the growth of credit and the positive performance of the Colombian economy.<sup id="cite_ref-strongmacroeconomicmanagement_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strongmacroeconomicmanagement-19">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[208]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[209]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Colombian Stock Exchange">Colombian Stock Exchange</a> through the Latin American Integrated Market (<a href="/wiki/Mercado_Integrado_Latinoamericano" title="Mercado Integrado Latinoamericano">MILA</a>) offers a regional market to trade equities.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[210]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[211]</a></sup> Colombia is now one of only three economies with a perfect score on the strength of legal rights index, according to the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[212]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:BVC_Bogota.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/BVC_Bogota.jpg/150px-BVC_Bogota.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/BVC_Bogota.jpg/225px-BVC_Bogota.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/BVC_Bogota.jpg/300px-BVC_Bogota.jpg 2x" data-file-width="928" data-file-height="1460"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:BVC_Bogota.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Colombian Stock Exchange">Colombian Stock Exchange</a> is part of the Latin American Integrated Market (<a href="/wiki/Mercado_Integrado_Latinoamericano" title="Mercado Integrado Latinoamericano">MILA</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-MILA_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MILA-220">[213]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The electricity production in Colombia comes mainly from <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">Renewable energy</a> sources. 69.93% is obtained from the <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectric generation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[214]</a></sup> Colombia's commitment to renewable energy was recognized in the 2014 <i>Global Green Economy Index (GGEI)</i>, ranking among the top 10 nations in the world in terms of greening efficiency sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-ggei_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ggei-222">[215]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Colombia is rich in natural resources, and its main exports include mineral fuels, oils, <a href="/wiki/Distillation#Industrial_distillation" title="Distillation">distillation products</a>, fruit and other agricultural products, sugars and sugar confectionery, <a href="/wiki/Food_products" class="mw-redirect" title="Food products">food products</a>, plastics, precious stones, metals, forest products, <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemical goods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceuticals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pharmaceuticals">pharmaceuticals</a>, vehicles, electronic products, electrical equipments, perfumery and cosmetics, machinery, manufactured articles, textile and fabrics, clothing and footwear, glass and glassware, furniture, prefabricated buildings, military products, home and office material, construction equipment, software, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-ITC_Colombia_Exports_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ITC_Colombia_Exports-223">[216]</a></sup> Principal trading partners are the United States, China, the European Union and some Latin American countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Exports_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Exports-224">[217]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Imports_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Imports-225">[218]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Non-traditional exports have boosted the growth of Colombian foreign sales as well as the diversification of destinations of export thanks to new <a href="/wiki/Free_trade_agreements" class="mw-redirect" title="Free trade agreements">free trade agreements</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[219]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, the National Administrative Department of Statistics (DANE) reported that 26.9% of the population were living below the poverty line, of which 7.4% in "extreme poverty". The multidimensional poverty rate stands at 17.0 percent of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-socio-economic_policies_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-socio-economic_policies-6">[6]</a></sup> The Government has also been developing a process of <a href="/wiki/Financial_inclusion" title="Financial inclusion">financial inclusion</a> within the country's most vulnerable population.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[220]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Recent economic growth has led to a considerable increase of new millionaires, including the new entrepreneurs, Colombians with a net worth exceeding US$1&nbsp;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[221]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[222]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The contribution of <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Colombia" title="Tourism in Colombia">Travel &amp; Tourism</a> to GDP was US$5,880.3bn (2.0% of total GDP) in 2016. Tourism generated 556,135 jobs (2.5% of total employment) in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[223]</a></sup> Foreign tourist visits were predicted to have risen from 0.6&nbsp;million in 2007 to 4&nbsp;million in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[224]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[225]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Colombia" title="Science and technology in Colombia">Science and technology in Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:CEMSA_271215_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/CEMSA_271215_01.JPG/200px-CEMSA_271215_01.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/CEMSA_271215_01.JPG/300px-CEMSA_271215_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/CEMSA_271215_01.JPG/400px-CEMSA_271215_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:CEMSA_271215_01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/COLCIENCIAS" class="mw-redirect" title="COLCIENCIAS">COLCIENCIAS</a> is a Colombian Government agency that supports fundamental and applied research.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Colombia has more than 3,950 research groups in science and technology.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[226]</a></sup> iNNpulsa, a government body that promotes entrepreneurship and innovation in the country, provides grants to startups, in addition to other services it and institutions like Apps.co provide. Co-working spaces have arisen to serve as communities for startups large and small.<sup id="cite_ref-venturebeat.com_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-venturebeat.com-234">[227]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[228]</a></sup> Organizations such as the Corporation for Biological Research (CIB) for the support of young people interested in scientific work has been successfully developed in Colombia.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[229]</a></sup> The International Center for Tropical Agriculture based in Colombia investigates the increasing challenge of <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" class="mw-redirect" title="Global warming">global warming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food security</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[230]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Important inventions related to medicine have been made in Colombia, such as the first <a href="/wiki/Artificial_cardiac_pacemaker" title="Artificial cardiac pacemaker">external artificial pacemaker with internal electrodes</a>, invented by the electronics engineer <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Reynolds_Pombo" title="Jorge Reynolds Pombo">Jorge Reynolds Pombo</a>, invention of great importance for those who suffer from heart failure. Also invented in Colombia were the <a href="/wiki/Microkeratome" title="Microkeratome">microkeratome</a> and keratomileusis technique, which form the fundamental basis of what now is known as <a href="/wiki/LASIK" title="LASIK">LASIK</a> (one of the most important techniques for the correction of <a href="/wiki/Refractive_error" title="Refractive error">refractive errors</a> of vision) and the <a href="/wiki/Salom%C3%B3n_Hakim#The_Invention_of_the_valve" title="Salomón Hakim">Hakim valve</a> for the treatment of <a href="/wiki/Hydrocephalus" title="Hydrocephalus">Hydrocephalus</a>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[231]</a></sup> Colombia has begun to innovate in military technology for its army and other armies of the world; especially in the design and creation of personal ballistic protection products, military hardware, <a href="/wiki/Military_robot" title="Military robot">military robots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bomb" title="Bomb">bombs</a>, simulators and radar.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[232]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[233]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[234]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Some leading Colombian scientists are Joseph M. Tohme, researcher recognized for his work on the <a href="/wiki/Genetic_diversity" title="Genetic diversity">genetic diversity</a> of food, Manuel Elkin Patarroyo who is known for his groundbreaking work on <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_vaccine" title="Synthetic vaccine">synthetic vaccines</a> for <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, Francisco Lopera who discovered the "Paisa Mutation" or a type of <a href="/wiki/Early-onset_Alzheimer%27s_disease" title="Early-onset Alzheimer's disease">early-onset Alzheimer's</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Francisco_Lopera_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Francisco_Lopera-242">[235]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rodolfo_Llin%C3%A1s" title="Rodolfo Llinás">Rodolfo Llinás</a> known for his study of the intrinsic <a href="/wiki/Neuron" title="Neuron">neurons</a> properties and the theory of a syndrome that had changed the way of understanding the functioning of the brain, Jairo Quiroga Puello recognized for his studies on the characterization of <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_substance" title="Synthetic substance">synthetic substances</a> which can be used to fight fungus, <a href="/wiki/Tumor" class="mw-redirect" title="Tumor">tumors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> and even some viruses and Ángela Restrepo who established accurate <a href="/wiki/Medical_diagnosis" title="Medical diagnosis">diagnoses</a> and treatments to combat the effects of a disease caused by the <i><a href="/wiki/Paracoccidioides_brasiliensis" title="Paracoccidioides brasiliensis">Paracoccidioides brasiliensis</a></i>, among other scientists.<sup id="cite_ref-Científicos_colombianos_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Científicos_colombianos-243">[236]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-brillantes_colombianos_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brillantes_colombianos-244">[237]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Científicos_destacados_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Científicos_destacados-245">[238]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Colombia" title="Transport in Colombia">Transport in Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cartagena2011-Skyline-Habour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Cartagena2011-Skyline-Habour.jpg/190px-Cartagena2011-Skyline-Habour.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Cartagena2011-Skyline-Habour.jpg/285px-Cartagena2011-Skyline-Habour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Cartagena2011-Skyline-Habour.jpg/380px-Cartagena2011-Skyline-Habour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cartagena2011-Skyline-Habour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Port of <a href="/wiki/Cartagena_de_Indias" class="mw-redirect" title="Cartagena de Indias">Cartagena</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Transportation in Colombia is regulated within the functions of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Transport_(Colombia)" title="Ministry of Transport (Colombia)">Ministry of Transport</a><sup id="cite_ref-MTransport_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTransport-246">[239]</a></sup> and entities such as the National Roads Institute (<a href="/wiki/INV%C3%8DAS" class="mw-redirect" title="INVÍAS">INVÍAS</a>) responsible for the <a href="/wiki/Highways_in_Colombia" title="Highways in Colombia">Highways in Colombia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[240]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Aerocivil" class="mw-redirect" title="Aerocivil">Aerocivil</a>, responsible for civil aviation and <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Colombia" title="List of airports in Colombia">airports</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[241]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/National_Infrastructure_Agency_(Colombia)" title="National Infrastructure Agency (Colombia)">National Infrastructure Agency</a>, in charge of <a href="/wiki/Concession_(contract)" title="Concession (contract)">concessions</a> through <a href="/wiki/Public%E2%80%93private_partnership" title="Public–private partnership">public–private partnerships</a>, for the design, construction, maintenance, operation, and administration of the transport infrastructure,<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[242]</a></sup> the General Maritime Directorate (Dimar) has the responsibility of coordinating maritime traffic control along with the Colombian Navy,<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[243]</a></sup> among others and under the supervision of the <a href="/wiki/Superintendency_of_Ports_and_Transport_(Colombia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Superintendency of Ports and Transport (Colombia)">Superintendency of Ports and Transport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[244]</a></sup> The road network in Colombia has a length of about 215,000&nbsp;km of which 23,000 are paved.<sup id="cite_ref-transporte_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transporte-252">[245]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Colombia" title="Rail transport in Colombia">Rail transportation</a> in Colombia is dedicated almost entirely to <a href="/wiki/Rail_freight_transport" title="Rail freight transport">freight shipments</a> and the railway network has a length of 1,700&nbsp;km of potentially active rails.<sup id="cite_ref-transporte_252-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transporte-252">[245]</a></sup> Colombia has 3,960 kilometers of gas pipelines, 4,900 kilometers of <a href="/wiki/Oil_pipelines" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil pipelines">oil pipelines</a>, and 2,990 kilometers of refined-products pipelines.<sup id="cite_ref-transporte_252-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transporte-252">[245]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The target of Colombia's government is to build 7,000&nbsp;km of roads for the 2016–2020 period and reduce travel times by 30 per cent and transport costs by 20 per cent. A toll road concession programme will comprise 40 projects, and is part of a larger strategic goal to invest nearly $50bn in transport infrastructure, including: railway systems; making the <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_river" class="mw-redirect" title="Magdalena river">Magdalena river</a> navigable again; improving port facilities; as well as an expansion of <a href="/wiki/El_Dorado_International_Airport" title="El Dorado International Airport">Bogotá's airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[246]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Colombia" title="Demographics of Colombia">Demographics of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Colombian_Departments_by_population" title="List of Colombian Departments by population">List of Colombian Departments by population</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Colombia_relief_demographic_map-fr.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Colombia_relief_demographic_map-fr.png/250px-Colombia_relief_demographic_map-fr.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="322" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Colombia_relief_demographic_map-fr.png/375px-Colombia_relief_demographic_map-fr.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Colombia_relief_demographic_map-fr.png/500px-Colombia_relief_demographic_map-fr.png 2x" data-file-width="1082" data-file-height="1394"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Colombia_relief_demographic_map-fr.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Population density of Colombia in 2007
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>With an estimated 50&nbsp;million people in 2020, Colombia is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by population">third-most populous country</a> in Latin America, after Brazil and Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-PopulationProjections_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopulationProjections-4">[4]</a></sup> At the beginning of the 20th century, Colombia's population was approximately 4&nbsp;million.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[247]</a></sup> Since the early 1970s Colombia has experienced steady declines in its fertility, mortality, and <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">population growth</a> rates. The population growth rate for 2016 is estimated to be 0.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-Population_growth_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population_growth-255">[248]</a></sup> About 26.8% of the population were 15 years old or younger, 65.7% were between 15 and 64 years old, and 7.4% were over 65 years old. The proportion of older persons in the total population has begun to increase substantially.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[249]</a></sup> Colombia is projected to have a population of 55.3&nbsp;million by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[250]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The population is concentrated in the <a href="/wiki/Andean_Region_of_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Andean Region of Colombia">Andean highlands</a> and along the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Region_of_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean Region of Colombia">Caribbean coast</a>, also the population densities are generally higher in the Andean region. The nine eastern lowland departments, comprising about 54% of Colombia's area, have less than 6% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-populationbyregions_149-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-populationbyregions-149">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Population_density_150-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Population_density-150">[143]</a></sup> Traditionally a rural society, <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">movement to urban areas</a> was very heavy in the mid-20th century, and Colombia is now one of the most urbanized countries in Latin America. The urban population increased from 31% of the total in 1938 to nearly 60% in 1973, and by 2014 the figure stood at 76%.<sup id="cite_ref-Country_Study_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Country_Study-258">[251]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[252]</a></sup> The population of <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogotá">Bogotá</a> alone has increased from just over 300,000 in 1938 to approximately 8&nbsp;million today.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[253]</a></sup> In total seventy-two cities now have populations of 100,000 or more (2015). As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Colombia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Colombia has the world's largest populations of <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">internally displaced persons</a> (IDPs), estimated to be up to 4.9&nbsp;million people.<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCR_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCR-261">[254]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The life expectancy is 74.8 years in 2015 and infant mortality is 13.1 per thousand in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-Life_expectancy_at_birth_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Life_expectancy_at_birth-262">[255]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-infant_mortality_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infant_mortality-263">[256]</a></sup> In 2015, 94.58% of adults and 98.66% of youth are literate and the government spends about 4.49% of its GDP on education.<sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO-264">[257]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Colombia" title="Languages of Colombia">Languages of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Spanish" title="Colombian Spanish">Colombian Spanish</a>
      </div> 
      <p>More than 99.2% of Colombians speak Spanish, also called Castilian; 65 <a href="/wiki/Amerindian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindian language">Amerindian languages</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Creole_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Creole languages">Creole languages</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani language</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Sign_Language" title="Colombian Sign Language">Colombian Sign Language</a> are also used in the country. <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> has official status in the <a href="/wiki/Archipelago_of_San_Andr%C3%A9s,_Providencia_and_Santa_Catalina" title="Archipelago of San Andrés, Providencia and Santa Catalina">archipelago of San Andrés, Providencia and Santa Catalina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LEY47DE1993_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LEY47DE1993-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lenguas_indígenas_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lenguas_indígenas-265">[258]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Languages_of_Colombia_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Languages_of_Colombia-266">[259]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MapofthelanguagesofColombia_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MapofthelanguagesofColombia-267">[260]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Including Spanish, a total of 101 languages are listed for Colombia in the <a href="/wiki/Ethnologue" title="Ethnologue">Ethnologue</a> database. The specific number of spoken languages varies slightly since some authors consider as different languages what others consider to be varieties or dialects of the same language. Best estimates recorded 71 languages that are spoken in-country today&nbsp;– most of which belong to the <a href="/wiki/Chibchan_languages" title="Chibchan languages">Chibchan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tucanoan_languages" title="Tucanoan languages">Tucanoan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bora%E2%80%93Witoto_languages" title="Bora–Witoto languages">Bora–Witoto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guajiboan_languages" title="Guajiboan languages">Guajiboan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arawakan_languages" title="Arawakan languages">Arawakan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cariban_languages" title="Cariban languages">Cariban</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbacoan_languages" title="Barbacoan languages">Barbacoan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Piaroa%E2%80%93Saliban_languages" title="Piaroa–Saliban languages">Saliban</a> language families. There are currently about 850,000 speakers of native languages.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnologue_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnologue-268">[261]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nativelanguages_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nativelanguages-269">[262]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_Colombia" title="Race and ethnicity in Colombia">Human biological diversity and ethnicity in Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"> 
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">

         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 265.14603691466px; border-left-color:#FFBF00"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:#FFBF00"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:#FFBF00"></div>

         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:#008080"></div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption"> 
         <p>Human biological diversity and ethnicity<sup id="cite_ref-grupos_étnicos_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grupos_étnicos-1">[1]</a></sup> </p> 
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#008080; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/White_Colombians" title="White Colombians">White</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mestizo_Colombians" title="Mestizo Colombians">Mestizo</a> (87.58%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#FFBF00; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Afro-Colombian" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Colombian">Afro-Colombian</a> (includes <a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">Mixed</a>) (6.68%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#1C39BB; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Colombia" title="Indigenous peoples in Colombia">Amerindian</a> (4.31%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#008080; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Not Stated (1.35%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#FFBF00; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Raizal" title="Raizal">Raizal</a> (0.06%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#008080; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Palenquero" title="Palenquero">Palenquero</a> (0.02%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#808080; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Romani_People" class="mw-redirect" title="Romani People">Romani</a> (0.01%)
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Colombia is ethnically diverse, its people descending from the original <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Colombia" title="Indigenous peoples in Colombia">native</a> inhabitants, Spanish colonists, <a href="/wiki/African_Colombian" class="mw-redirect" title="African Colombian">Africans</a> originally brought to the country as slaves, and 20th-century <a href="/wiki/European_diaspora" class="mw-redirect" title="European diaspora">immigrants from Europe</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Colombians" title="Arab Colombians">Middle East</a>, all contributing to a diverse cultural heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-Colombia_is_ethnically_diverse_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombia_is_ethnically_diverse-270">[263]</a></sup> The demographic distribution reflects a pattern that is influenced by colonial history.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[264]</a></sup> Whites live all throughout the country, mainly in urban centers and the burgeoning highland and coastal cities. The populations of the major cities also include mestizos. <a href="/wiki/Mestizo_Colombian" class="mw-redirect" title="Mestizo Colombian">Mestizo</a> <i>campesinos</i> (people living in rural areas) also live in the Andean highlands where some Spanish conquerors mixed with the women of Amerindian <a href="/wiki/Chiefdoms" class="mw-redirect" title="Chiefdoms">chiefdoms</a>. Mestizos include artisans and small tradesmen that have played a major part in the urban expansion of recent decades.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[265]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/2018_Colombian_Census" title="2018 Colombian Census">2018 census</a> reported that the "non-ethnic population", consisting of <a href="/wiki/White_Colombian" class="mw-redirect" title="White Colombian">whites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mestizo_Colombian" class="mw-redirect" title="Mestizo Colombian">mestizos</a> (those of mixed European and Amerindian ancestry), constituted 87.58% of the national population. 6.68% is of <a href="/wiki/Afro-Colombian" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Colombian">African</a> ancestry. <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Colombia" title="Indigenous peoples in Colombia">Indigenous Amerindians</a> constitute 4.31% of the population. <a href="/wiki/Raizal" title="Raizal">Raizal</a> people constitute 0.06% of the population. <a href="/wiki/Palenquero" title="Palenquero">Palenquero</a> people constitute 0.02% of the population. 0.01% of the population are <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Roma</a>. An extraofficial estimate considers that the 49% of the Colombian population is <a href="/wiki/Mestizo_Colombian" class="mw-redirect" title="Mestizo Colombian">Mestizo</a> or of mixed European and Amerindian ancestry, and that approximately 37% is <a href="/wiki/White_Colombian" class="mw-redirect" title="White Colombian">White</a>, mainly of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_immigration_to_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish immigration to Colombia">Spanish</a> lineage, but there is also a large population of <a href="/wiki/Arab_Colombians" title="Arab Colombians">Middle East</a> descent; in some sectors of society there is a considerable input of <a href="/wiki/German_Colombian" title="German Colombian">German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Colombian" title="Italian Colombian">Italian</a> ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Society_and_Its_Environment_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Society_and_Its_Environment-273">[266]</a></sup> </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:308px;max-width:308px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Mapa_de_Colombia_(poblaci%C3%B3n_afrodescendiente_2005).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Mapa_de_Colombia_%28poblaci%C3%B3n_afrodescendiente_2005%29.svg/150px-Mapa_de_Colombia_%28poblaci%C3%B3n_afrodescendiente_2005%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="203" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Mapa_de_Colombia_%28poblaci%C3%B3n_afrodescendiente_2005%29.svg/225px-Mapa_de_Colombia_%28poblaci%C3%B3n_afrodescendiente_2005%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Mapa_de_Colombia_%28poblaci%C3%B3n_afrodescendiente_2005%29.svg/300px-Mapa_de_Colombia_%28poblaci%C3%B3n_afrodescendiente_2005%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="3731" data-file-height="5050"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           People with <a href="/wiki/African_Colombian" class="mw-redirect" title="African Colombian">African ancestry</a> in Colombia are concentrated mostly in coastal areas.
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Mapa_de_Colombia_(poblaci%C3%B3n_ind%C3%ADgena_2005).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Mapa_de_Colombia_%28poblaci%C3%B3n_ind%C3%ADgena_2005%29.svg/150px-Mapa_de_Colombia_%28poblaci%C3%B3n_ind%C3%ADgena_2005%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="203" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Mapa_de_Colombia_%28poblaci%C3%B3n_ind%C3%ADgena_2005%29.svg/225px-Mapa_de_Colombia_%28poblaci%C3%B3n_ind%C3%ADgena_2005%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Mapa_de_Colombia_%28poblaci%C3%B3n_ind%C3%ADgena_2005%29.svg/300px-Mapa_de_Colombia_%28poblaci%C3%B3n_ind%C3%ADgena_2005%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="3731" data-file-height="5050"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Colombia" title="Indigenous peoples in Colombia">Amerindian</a> population of Colombia by municipality in 2005.
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Many of the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Colombia" title="Indigenous peoples in Colombia">Indigenous peoples</a> experienced a reduction in population during the Spanish rule<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[267]</a></sup> and many others were absorbed into the mestizo population, but the remainder currently represents over eighty distinct cultures.
