Reserves (<i>resguardos</i>) established for indigenous peoples occupy 30,571,640 hectares (305,716.4&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) (27% of the country's total) and are inhabited by more than 800,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-Resguardos_Indígenas_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Resguardos_Indígenas-275">[268]</a></sup> Some of the largest indigenous groups are the <a href="/wiki/Wayuu" class="mw-redirect" title="Wayuu">Wayuu</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-wayuu_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wayuu-276">[269]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Paez_people" title="Paez people">Paez</a>, the Pastos, the <a href="/wiki/Ember%C3%A1_people" title="Emberá people">Emberá</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Zen%C3%BA" title="Zenú">Zenú</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pueblos_indígenas_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pueblos_indígenas-277">[270]</a></sup> The departments of <a href="/wiki/Department_of_La_Guajira" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of La Guajira">La Guajira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cauca_Department" title="Cauca Department">Cauca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nari%C3%B1o_Department" title="Nariño Department">Nariño</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba_Department" title="Córdoba Department">Córdoba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sucre_Department" title="Sucre Department">Sucre</a> have the largest indigenous populations.<sup id="cite_ref-grupos_étnicos_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grupos_étnicos-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Indigenous_Organization_of_Colombia" title="National Indigenous Organization of Colombia">Organización Nacional Indígena de Colombia</a> (ONIC), founded at the first National Indigenous Congress in 1982, is an organization representing the indigenous peoples of Colombia. In 1991, Colombia signed and ratified the current international law concerning indigenous peoples, <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_and_Tribal_Peoples_Convention,_1989" title="Indigenous and Tribal Peoples Convention, 1989">Indigenous and Tribal Peoples Convention, 1989</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ratifications_-_ilo.org_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ratifications_-_ilo.org-278">[271]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africans" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-Saharan Africans">Sub-Saharan Africans</a> were brought as <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">slaves</a>, mostly to the coastal lowlands, beginning early in the 16th century and continuing into the 19th century. Large Afro-Colombian communities are found today on the Pacific Coast.<sup id="cite_ref-Grupos_Étnicos_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grupos_Étnicos-279">[272]</a></sup> Numerous <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Jamaican people">Jamaicans</a> migrated mainly to the islands of San Andres and Providencia. A number of other Europeans and North Americans migrated to the country in the late 19th and early 20th centuries, including people from the former <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">USSR</a> during and after the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Extranjeros_en_Colombia_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Extranjeros_en_Colombia-280">[273]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Migraciones_Internacionales_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Migraciones_Internacionales-281">[274]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Many immigrant communities have settled on the Caribbean coast, in particular recent immigrants from the <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_West_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic groups in West Asia">Middle East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. Barranquilla (the largest city of the Colombian Caribbean) and other Caribbean cities have the largest populations of <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Colombian" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanese Colombian">Lebanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Arab_Colombians" title="Arab Colombians">Levantines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-arab_colombians_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arab_colombians-282">[275]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[276]</a></sup> There are also important communities of Chinese, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Colombian" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Colombian">Japanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romanis</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Colombia" title="History of the Jews in Colombia">Jews</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Colombia_is_ethnically_diverse_270-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombia_is_ethnically_diverse-270">[263]</a></sup> There is a major migration trend of <a href="/wiki/Venezuelan_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Venezuelan people">Venezuelans</a>, due to the political and economic situation in Venezuela.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[277]</a></sup> In August 2019, Colombia offered citizenship to more than 24,000 children of Venezuelan refugees who were born in Colombia.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[278]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Colombia" title="Religion in Colombia">Religion in Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion_in_Colombia" title="Freedom of religion in Colombia">Freedom of religion in Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jews_in_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Jews in Colombia">Jews in Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Santuario_de_Las_Lajas,_Ipiales,_Colombia,_2015-07-21,_DD_21-23_HDR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Santuario_de_Las_Lajas%2C_Ipiales%2C_Colombia%2C_2015-07-21%2C_DD_21-23_HDR.jpg/220px-Santuario_de_Las_Lajas%2C_Ipiales%2C_Colombia%2C_2015-07-21%2C_DD_21-23_HDR.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Santuario_de_Las_Lajas%2C_Ipiales%2C_Colombia%2C_2015-07-21%2C_DD_21-23_HDR.jpg/330px-Santuario_de_Las_Lajas%2C_Ipiales%2C_Colombia%2C_2015-07-21%2C_DD_21-23_HDR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Santuario_de_Las_Lajas%2C_Ipiales%2C_Colombia%2C_2015-07-21%2C_DD_21-23_HDR.jpg/440px-Santuario_de_Las_Lajas%2C_Ipiales%2C_Colombia%2C_2015-07-21%2C_DD_21-23_HDR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3958" data-file-height="2758"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Santuario_de_Las_Lajas,_Ipiales,_Colombia,_2015-07-21,_DD_21-23_HDR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Las_Lajas_Sanctuary" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Lajas Sanctuary">Las Lajas Sanctuary</a> in the southern Colombian Department of <a href="/wiki/Nari%C3%B1o_Department" title="Nariño Department">Nariño</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Administrative_Department_of_Statistics" class="mw-redirect" title="National Administrative Department of Statistics">National Administrative Department of Statistics</a> (DANE) does not collect religious statistics, and accurate reports are difficult to obtain. However, based on various studies and a survey, about 90% of the population adheres to Christianity, the majority of which (70.9%–79%) are <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>, while a significant minority (16.7%) adhere to <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a> (primarily <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelicalism</a>). Some 4.7% of the population is <a href="/wiki/Atheist" class="mw-redirect" title="Atheist">atheist</a> or agnostic, while 3.5% claim to believe in God but do not follow a specific religion. 1.8% of Colombians adhere to <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adventism" title="Adventism">Adventism</a> and less than 1% adhere to other religions, such as the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, Judaism, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mormonism" title="Mormonism">Mormonism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">Indigenous religions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hare_Krishna_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Hare Krishna movement">Hare Krishna movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rastafari_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Rastafari movement">Rastafari movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Catholic Church">Orthodox Catholic Church</a>, and spiritual studies. The remaining people either did not respond or replied that they did not know. In addition to the above statistics, 35.9% of Colombians reported that they did not practice their faith actively.<sup id="cite_ref-Religion_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Religion-286">[279]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Religion2_287-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Religion2-287">[280]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Religion_in_Latin_America_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Religion_in_Latin_America-288">[281]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>While Colombia remains a mostly Roman Catholic country by <a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">baptism</a> numbers, the 1991 Colombian constitution guarantees freedom of religion and all religious faiths and churches are equally free before the law.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[282]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Culture of Colombia">Culture of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Festivals_in_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Festivals in Colombia">Festivals in Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colombian_folklore" title="Colombian folklore">Colombian folklore</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Colombia lies at the crossroads of <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_culture" title="Latin American culture">Latin America</a> and the broader American continent, and as such has been hit by a wide range of cultural influences. <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native American</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Spain" title="Culture of Spain">Spanish</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Europe" title="Culture of Europe">European</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Africa" title="Culture of Africa">African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_States" title="Culture of the United States">American</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Caribbean" title="Culture of the Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arab_culture" title="Arab culture">Middle Eastern</a> influences, as well as other Latin American cultural influences, are all present in Colombia's modern culture. Urban migration, industrialization, globalization, and other political, social and economic changes have also left an impression. </p>
      <p>Many <a href="/wiki/National_symbols_of_Colombia" title="National symbols of Colombia">national symbols</a>, both objects and themes, have arisen from Colombia's diverse cultural traditions and aim to represent what Colombia, and the Colombian people, have in common. Cultural expressions in Colombia are promoted by the government through the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Culture_(Colombia)" title="Ministry of Culture (Colombia)">Ministry of Culture</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Colombian_literature" title="Colombian literature">Colombian literature</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gabriel_Garcia_Marquez,_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Gabriel_Garcia_Marquez%2C_2009.jpg/220px-Gabriel_Garcia_Marquez%2C_2009.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Gabriel_Garcia_Marquez%2C_2009.jpg/330px-Gabriel_Garcia_Marquez%2C_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Gabriel_Garcia_Marquez%2C_2009.jpg/440px-Gabriel_Garcia_Marquez%2C_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1820" data-file-height="1658"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gabriel_Garcia_Marquez,_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_in_Literature" title="List of Nobel laureates in Literature">Nobel literature</a> prize winner <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Garc%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1rquez" title="Gabriel García Márquez">Gabriel García Márquez</a><sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[283]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Colombian literature dates back to pre-Columbian era; a notable example of the period is the epic poem known as the <i>Legend of Yurupary</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Legend_of_Yurupary_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Legend_of_Yurupary-291">[284]</a></sup> In Spanish colonial times, notable writers include <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Castellanos" title="Juan de Castellanos">Juan de Castellanos</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Eleg%C3%ADas_de_varones_ilustres_de_Indias" title="Elegías de varones ilustres de Indias">Elegías de varones ilustres de Indias</a></i>), Hernando Domínguez Camargo and his epic poem to San Ignacio de Loyola, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Sim%C3%B3n" title="Pedro Simón">Pedro Simón</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Freyle" title="Juan Rodríguez Freyle">Juan Rodríguez Freyle</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/El_Carnero" title="El Carnero">El Carnero</a></i>),<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[285]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Piedrahita" title="Lucas Fernández de Piedrahita">Lucas Fernández de Piedrahita</a>, and the nun <a href="/wiki/Francisca_Josefa_de_la_Concepci%C3%B3n" title="Francisca Josefa de la Concepción">Francisca Josefa de Castillo</a>, representative of <a href="/wiki/Mysticism" title="Mysticism">mysticism</a>. </p>
      <p>Post-independence literature linked to Romanticism highlighted <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Nari%C3%B1o" title="Antonio Nariño">Antonio Nariño</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Fern%C3%A1ndez_Madrid" title="José Fernández Madrid">José Fernández Madrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camilo_Torres_Tenorio" title="Camilo Torres Tenorio">Camilo Torres Tenorio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Antonio_Zea" title="Francisco Antonio Zea">Francisco Antonio Zea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[286]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[287]</a></sup> In the second half of the nineteenth century and early twentieth century the literary genre known as <i><a href="/wiki/Costumbrismo" title="Costumbrismo">costumbrismo</a></i> became popular; great writers of this period were <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_Carrasquilla" title="Tomás Carrasquilla">Tomás Carrasquilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Isaacs" title="Jorge Isaacs">Jorge Isaacs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Pombo" title="Rafael Pombo">Rafael Pombo</a> (the latter of whom wrote notable works of children's literature).<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[288]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[289]</a></sup> Within that period, authors such as <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Asunci%C3%B3n_Silva" title="José Asunción Silva">José Asunción Silva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Eustasio_Rivera" title="José Eustasio Rivera">José Eustasio Rivera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n_de_Greiff" title="León de Greiff">León de Greiff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porfirio_Barba-Jacob" title="Porfirio Barba-Jacob">Porfirio Barba-Jacob</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Vargas_Vila" title="José María Vargas Vila">José María Vargas Vila</a> developed the <a href="/wiki/Modernismo" title="Modernismo">modernist</a> movement.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[290]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[291]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[292]</a></sup> In 1872, Colombia established the <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Academy_of_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Colombian Academy of Language">Colombian Academy of Language</a>, the first Spanish language academy in the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[293]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Candelario_Obeso" title="Candelario Obeso">Candelario Obeso</a> wrote the groundbreaking <i>Cantos Populares de mi Tierra</i> (1877), the first book of poetry by an Afro-Colombian author.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[294]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Candelario_Obeso_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Candelario_Obeso-302">[295]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Between 1939 and 1940 seven books of poetry were published under the name <i><a href="/wiki/Stone_and_Sky_(movement)" title="Stone and Sky (movement)">Stone and Sky</a></i> in the city of Bogotá that significantly impacted the country; they were edited by the poet Jorge Rojas.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[296]</a></sup> In the following decade, <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Arango" title="Gonzalo Arango">Gonzalo Arango</a> founded the movement of "<a href="/wiki/Nadaism" title="Nadaism">nothingness</a>" in response to the violence of the time;<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[297]</a></sup> he was influenced by <a href="/wiki/Nihilism" title="Nihilism">nihilism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Existentialism" title="Existentialism">existentialism</a>, and the thought of another great Colombian writer: <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Gonz%C3%A1lez_(writer)" title="Fernando González (writer)">Fernando González Ochoa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">[298]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Boom" title="Latin American Boom">boom in Latin American literature</a>, successful writers emerged, led by <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel laureate</a> <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Garc%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1rquez" title="Gabriel García Márquez">Gabriel García Márquez</a> and his magnum opus, <i><a href="/wiki/One_Hundred_Years_of_Solitude" title="One Hundred Years of Solitude">One Hundred Years of Solitude</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Caballero_Calder%C3%B3n" title="Eduardo Caballero Calderón">Eduardo Caballero Calderón</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Mej%C3%ADa_Vallejo" title="Manuel Mejía Vallejo">Manuel Mejía Vallejo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_Mutis" title="Álvaro Mutis">Álvaro Mutis</a>, a writer who was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Cervantes_Prize" title="Miguel de Cervantes Prize">Cervantes Prize</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Asturias_Award_for_Letters" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince of Asturias Award for Letters">Prince of Asturias Award for Letters</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[299]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">[300]</a></sup> Other leading contemporary authors are <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Vallejo" title="Fernando Vallejo">Fernando Vallejo</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Ospina" title="William Ospina">William Ospina</a> (<a href="/wiki/R%C3%B3mulo_Gallegos_Prize" title="Rómulo Gallegos Prize">Rómulo Gallegos Prize</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Germ%C3%A1n_Castro_Caycedo" title="Germán Castro Caycedo">Germán Castro Caycedo</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_arts">Visual arts</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Colombian_art" title="Colombian art">Colombian art</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:184px;max-width:184px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:AdamandEve-FernandoBotero-20100414.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/AdamandEve-FernandoBotero-20100414.jpg/180px-AdamandEve-FernandoBotero-20100414.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="130" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/AdamandEve-FernandoBotero-20100414.jpg/270px-AdamandEve-FernandoBotero-20100414.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/AdamandEve-FernandoBotero-20100414.jpg/360px-AdamandEve-FernandoBotero-20100414.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2965" data-file-height="2136"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Work of the painter, and sculptor <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Botero" title="Fernando Botero">Fernando Botero</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Santiago_Martinez_Delgado_in_the_colombian_congress.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Santiago_Martinez_Delgado_in_the_colombian_congress.jpg/180px-Santiago_Martinez_Delgado_in_the_colombian_congress.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Santiago_Martinez_Delgado_in_the_colombian_congress.jpg/270px-Santiago_Martinez_Delgado_in_the_colombian_congress.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/28/Santiago_Martinez_Delgado_in_the_colombian_congress.jpg 2x" data-file-width="330" data-file-height="275"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Mural by <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Mart%C3%ADnez_Delgado" title="Santiago Martínez Delgado">Santiago Martínez Delgado</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Colombian art has over 3,000 years of history. Colombian artists have captured the country's changing political and cultural backdrop using a range of styles and mediums. There is archeological evidence of ceramics being produced earlier in Colombia than anywhere else in the Americas, dating as early as 3,000&nbsp;BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-donquijote.org_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-donquijote.org-308">[301]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-artecolombiano_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-artecolombiano-309">[302]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The earliest examples of gold craftsmanship have been attributed to the Tumaco people<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">[303]</a></sup> of the Pacific coast and date to around 325&nbsp;BCE. Roughly between 200&nbsp;BCE and 800 CE, the <a href="/wiki/San_Agust%C3%ADn,_Huila" title="San Agustín, Huila">San Agustín culture</a>, masters of <a href="/wiki/Stonemasonry" title="Stonemasonry">stonecutting</a>, entered its "classical period". They erected raised <a href="/wiki/Ceremony" title="Ceremony">ceremonial</a> centres, <a href="/wiki/Sarcophagi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sarcophagi">sarcophagi</a>, and large stone <a href="/wiki/Monolith" title="Monolith">monoliths</a> depicting <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphic" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthropomorphic">anthropomorphic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zoomorphism" title="Zoomorphism">zoomorphic</a> forms out of <a href="/wiki/Rock_(geology)" title="Rock (geology)">stone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-artecolombiano_309-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-artecolombiano-309">[302]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-San_Agustín_311-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-San_Agustín-311">[304]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Colombian art has followed the trends of the time, so during the 16th to 18th centuries, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Spain">Spanish Catholicism</a> had a huge influence on Colombian art, and the popular <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">baroque</a> style was replaced with <a href="/wiki/Rococo" title="Rococo">rococo</a> when the Bourbons ascended to the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">Spanish crown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">[305]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">[306]</a></sup> More recently, Colombian artists <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Nel_G%C3%B3mez" title="Pedro Nel Gómez">Pedro Nel Gómez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Mart%C3%ADnez_Delgado" title="Santiago Martínez Delgado">Santiago Martínez Delgado</a> started the Colombian Murial Movement in the 1940s, featuring the <a href="/wiki/Neoclassicism" title="Neoclassicism">neoclassical</a> features of <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-donquijote.org_308-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-donquijote.org-308">[301]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-artecolombiano_309-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-artecolombiano-309">[302]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">[307]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">[308]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Monumento_pantano_de_vargas,_completo._2006.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Monumento_pantano_de_vargas%2C_completo._2006.JPG/220px-Monumento_pantano_de_vargas%2C_completo._2006.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Monumento_pantano_de_vargas%2C_completo._2006.JPG/330px-Monumento_pantano_de_vargas%2C_completo._2006.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Monumento_pantano_de_vargas%2C_completo._2006.JPG/440px-Monumento_pantano_de_vargas%2C_completo._2006.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Monumento_pantano_de_vargas,_completo._2006.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Vargas_Swamp_Lancers" title="Vargas Swamp Lancers">Vargas Swamp Lancers</a>, artwork by <a href="/wiki/Rodrigo_Arenas_Betancourt" title="Rodrigo Arenas Betancourt">Rodrigo Arenas Betancourt</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since the 1950s, the Colombian art started to have a distinctive point of view, reinventing traditional elements under the concepts of the 20th century. Examples of this are the Greiff <a href="/wiki/Portrait" title="Portrait">portraits</a> by <a href="/wiki/Ignacio_G%C3%B3mez_Jaramillo" title="Ignacio Gómez Jaramillo">Ignacio Gómez Jaramillo</a>, showing what the Colombian art could do with the new techniques applied to typical Colombian themes. Carlos Correa, with his <a href="/wiki/Paradigm" title="Paradigm">paradigmatic</a> "Naturaleza muerta en silencio" (silent dead nature), combines geometrical <a href="/wiki/Abstraction_(art)" title="Abstraction (art)">abstraction</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cubism" title="Cubism">cubism</a>. <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Obreg%C3%B3n" title="Alejandro Obregón">Alejandro Obregón</a> is often considered as the father of modern Colombian painting, and one of the most influential artist in this period, due to his originality, the painting of Colombian landscapes with <a href="/wiki/Symbolism_(arts)" title="Symbolism (arts)">symbolic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Expressionism" title="Expressionism">expressionist</a> use of animals, (specially the <a href="/wiki/Andean_condor" title="Andean condor">Andean condor</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-artecolombiano_309-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-artecolombiano-309">[302]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">[309]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">[310]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Botero" title="Fernando Botero">Fernando Botero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Omar_Rayo" title="Omar Rayo">Omar Rayo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Grau" title="Enrique Grau">Enrique Grau</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89dgar_Negret" title="Édgar Negret">Édgar Negret</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Manzur" title="David Manzur">David Manzur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rodrigo_Arenas_Betancourt" title="Rodrigo Arenas Betancourt">Rodrigo Arenas Betancourt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Murillo_(artist)" title="Oscar Murillo (artist)">Oscar Murillo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doris_Salcedo" title="Doris Salcedo">Doris Salcedo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Mu%C3%B1oz_(artist)" title="Oscar Muñoz (artist)">Oscar Muñoz</a> are some of the Colombian artists featured at the international level.<sup id="cite_ref-donquijote.org_308-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-donquijote.org-308">[301]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">[311]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">[312]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-museorayo_320-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-museorayo-320">[313]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Colombian sculpture from the sixteenth to 18th centuries was mostly devoted to <a href="/wiki/Religious_art" title="Religious art">religious depictions</a> of ecclesiastic art, strongly influenced by the Spanish schools of <a href="/wiki/Sacred" title="Sacred">sacred</a> sculpture. During the early period of the Colombian republic, the national artists were focused in the production of sculptural portraits of politicians and public figures, in a plain <a href="/wiki/Neoclassicist" class="mw-redirect" title="Neoclassicist">neoclassicist</a> trend.<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">[314]</a></sup> During the 20th century, the Colombian sculpture began to develop a bold and innovative work with the aim of reaching a better understanding of national sensitivity.<sup id="cite_ref-artecolombiano_309-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-artecolombiano-309">[302]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_sculptors_322-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_sculptors-322">[315]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Colombian photography was marked by the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Daguerreotype" title="Daguerreotype">daguerreotype</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Louis_Gros" class="mw-redirect" title="Jean-Baptiste Louis Gros">Jean-Baptiste Louis Gros</a> was who brought the daguerreotype process to Colombia in 1841. The Piloto public library has Latin America's largest archive of negatives, containing 1.7&nbsp;million antique photographs covering Colombia 1848 until 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">[316]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">[317]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Colombian press has promoted the work of the <a href="/wiki/Cartoonist" title="Cartoonist">cartoonists</a>. In recent decades, <a href="/wiki/Fanzine" title="Fanzine">fanzines</a>, internet and <a href="/wiki/Independent_publisher" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent publisher">independent publishers</a> have been fundamental to the growth of the comic in Colombia.<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">[318]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">[319]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">[320]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Colombia" title="Architecture of Colombia">Architecture of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Muisca_architecture" title="Muisca architecture">Muisca architecture</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Throughout the times, there have been a variety of <a href="/wiki/List_of_architectural_styles" title="List of architectural styles">architectural styles</a>, from those of indigenous peoples to contemporary ones, passing through colonial (military and religious), Republican, transition and modern styles.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">[321]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Santa_B%C3%A1rbara_-_Momp%C3%B3s.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Santa_B%C3%A1rbara_-_Momp%C3%B3s.jpg/220px-Santa_B%C3%A1rbara_-_Momp%C3%B3s.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Santa_B%C3%A1rbara_-_Momp%C3%B3s.jpg/330px-Santa_B%C3%A1rbara_-_Momp%C3%B3s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Santa_B%C3%A1rbara_-_Momp%C3%B3s.jpg/440px-Santa_B%C3%A1rbara_-_Momp%C3%B3s.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1182" data-file-height="771"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Santa_B%C3%A1rbara_-_Momp%C3%B3s.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Historic Centre of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Mompox" title="Santa Cruz de Mompox">Santa Cruz de Mompox</a>, an architectural site with colonial elements
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ancient habitation areas, longhouses, <a href="/wiki/Terrace_(agriculture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Terrace (agriculture)">crop terraces</a>, roads as the <a href="/wiki/Inca_road_system" title="Inca road system">Inca road system</a>, cemeteries, <a href="/wiki/Hypogeum" title="Hypogeum">hypogeums</a> and <a href="/wiki/Necropolis" title="Necropolis">necropolises</a> are all part of the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_architecture" title="Indigenous architecture">architectural heritage of indigenous peoples</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">[322]</a></sup> Some prominent indigenous structures are the <a href="/wiki/Andean_preceramic" title="Andean preceramic">preceramic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ceramic" title="Ceramic">ceramic</a> archaeological site of <a href="/wiki/Tequendama" title="Tequendama">Tequendama</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">[323]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tierradentro" title="Tierradentro">Tierradentro</a> (a park that contains the largest concentration of <a href="/wiki/List_of_pre-Columbian_cultures" title="List of pre-Columbian cultures">pre-Columbian</a> monumental <a href="/wiki/Shaft_tomb" title="Shaft tomb">shaft tombs</a> with side chambers),<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">[324]</a></sup> the largest collection of religious monuments and <a href="/wiki/Megalithic" class="mw-redirect" title="Megalithic">megalithic</a> sculptures in South America, located in <a href="/wiki/San_Agust%C3%ADn_Archaeological_Park" title="San Agustín Archaeological Park">San Agustín, Huila</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-San_Agustín_311-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-San_Agustín-311">[304]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">[325]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Perdida" title="Ciudad Perdida">Lost city</a> (an archaeological site with a series of terraces carved into the mountainside, a net of tiled roads, and several circular plazas), and the large villages mainly built with <a href="/wiki/Stone" class="mw-redirect" title="Stone">stone</a>, wood, cane, and mud.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">[326]</a></sup> Architecture during the period of conquest and colonization is mainly derived of adapting <a href="/wiki/European_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="European architecture">European styles</a> to local conditions, and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_architecture" title="Spanish architecture">Spanish influence</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">Extremaduran</a>, can be easily seen.<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">[327]</a></sup> When Europeans founded cities two things were making simultaneously: the dimensioning of geometrical space (<a href="/wiki/Town_square" title="Town square">town square</a>, street), and the location of a tangible point of <a href="/wiki/Map_orientation" class="mw-redirect" title="Map orientation">orientation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">[328]</a></sup> The construction of <a href="/wiki/Fort" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort">forts</a> was common throughout the Caribbean and in some cities of the interior, because of the dangers posed to Spanish colonial settlements from English, French and Dutch <a href="/wiki/Piracy_in_the_Caribbean" title="Piracy in the Caribbean">pirates</a> and hostile indigenous groups.<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">[329]</a></sup> Churches, chapels, schools, and hospitals belonging to <a href="/wiki/Catholic_religious_order" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic religious order">religious orders</a> cause a great urban impact.<sup id="cite_ref-1550–1750_337-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1550–1750-337">[330]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque architecture</a> is used in military buildings and public spaces.<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">[331]</a></sup> Marcelino Arroyo, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Jos%C3%A9_de_Caldas" title="Francisco José de Caldas">Francisco José de Caldas</a> and Domingo de Petrés were great representatives of <a href="/wiki/Neo-classical_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-classical architecture">neo-classical architecture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1550–1750_337-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1550–1750-337">[330]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:240px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Plaza_Villa_de_Leyva.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Plaza_Villa_de_Leyva.jpg/238px-Plaza_Villa_de_Leyva.jpg" decoding="async" width="238" height="105" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Plaza_Villa_de_Leyva.jpg/357px-Plaza_Villa_de_Leyva.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Plaza_Villa_de_Leyva.jpg/476px-Plaza_Villa_de_Leyva.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="2420"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Plaza_Villa_de_Leyva.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Central plaza of the colonial town of <a href="/wiki/Villa_de_Leyva" title="Villa de Leyva">Villa de Leyva</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Capitolio_Nacional" title="Capitolio Nacional">National Capitol</a> is a great representative of romanticism.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">[332]</a></sup> Wood was extensively used in doors, windows, railings, and ceilings during the colonization of <a href="/wiki/Antioquia_Department" title="Antioquia Department">Antioquia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_region_of_Colombia" title="Caribbean region of Colombia">Caribbean</a> architecture acquires a strong <a href="/wiki/Arabic_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic architecture">Arabic influence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">[333]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Teatro_de_Crist%C3%B3bal_Col%C3%B3n" title="Teatro de Cristóbal Colón">Teatro Colón</a> in Bogotá is a lavish example of architecture from the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">[334]</a></sup> The quintas houses with innovations in the <a href="/wiki/Volumetric" class="mw-redirect" title="Volumetric">volumetric</a> conception are some of the best examples of the Republican architecture; the Republican action in the city focused on the design of three types of <a href="/wiki/Spatial_analysis" title="Spatial analysis">spaces</a>: parks with forests, small <a href="/wiki/Urban_park" title="Urban park">urban parks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Avenue_(landscape)" title="Avenue (landscape)">avenues</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic style</a> was most commonly used for the design of churches.<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">[335]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Deco style, <a href="/wiki/Rationalism_(architecture)" title="Rationalism (architecture)">modern neoclassicism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eclecticism_in_architecture" title="Eclecticism in architecture">eclecticism</a> <a href="/wiki/Folklorist" class="mw-redirect" title="Folklorist">folklorist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Art_deco" class="mw-redirect" title="Art deco">art deco</a> <a href="/wiki/Ornament_(art)" title="Ornament (art)">ornamental</a> resources significantly influenced the architecture of Colombia, especially during the transition period.<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">[336]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/International_Style_(architecture)" title="International Style (architecture)">Modernism</a> contributed with new construction technologies and new <a href="/wiki/Building_material" title="Building material">materials</a> (steel, <a href="/wiki/Reinforced_concrete" title="Reinforced concrete">reinforced concrete</a>, glass and synthetic materials) and the <a href="/wiki/Topology" title="Topology">topology</a> architecture and <a href="/wiki/Concrete_slab" title="Concrete slab">lightened slabs system</a> also have a great influence.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">[337]</a></sup> The most influential architects of the modern movement were <a href="/wiki/Rogelio_Salmona" title="Rogelio Salmona">Rogelio Salmona</a> and Fernando Martínez Sanabria.<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">[338]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_architecture" title="Contemporary architecture">contemporary architecture</a> of Colombia is designed to give greater importance to the <a href="/wiki/Building_material" title="Building material">materials</a>, this architecture takes into account the specific <a href="/wiki/Geographical_feature" title="Geographical feature">natural and artificial geographies</a> and is also an architecture that appeals to the <a href="/wiki/Sense" title="Sense">senses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">[339]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Architectural_conservation" title="Architectural conservation">conservation of the architectural and urban heritage</a> of Colombia has been promoted in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">[340]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Colombia" title="Music of Colombia">Music of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:330px;max-width:330px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:177px;max-width:177px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Ejes_musicales_de_Colombia1.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Ejes_musicales_de_Colombia1.png/175px-Ejes_musicales_de_Colombia1.png" decoding="async" width="175" height="308" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Ejes_musicales_de_Colombia1.png/263px-Ejes_musicales_de_Colombia1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Ejes_musicales_de_Colombia1.png/350px-Ejes_musicales_de_Colombia1.png 2x" data-file-width="7180" data-file-height="12642"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Colombia" title="Music of Colombia">Musical Regions</a> of Colombia.
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:149px;max-width:149px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Tiple.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Tiple.jpg/147px-Tiple.jpg" decoding="async" width="147" height="307" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Tiple.jpg/221px-Tiple.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Tiple.jpg/294px-Tiple.jpg 2x" data-file-width="921" data-file-height="1926"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Colombian_tiple" title="Colombian tiple">Colombian tiple</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Colombia has a vibrant collage of talent that touches a full spectrum of <a href="/wiki/Rhythm" title="Rhythm">rhythms</a>. Musicians, composers, music producers and singers from Colombia are recognized internationally such as <a href="/wiki/Shakira" title="Shakira">Shakira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juanes" title="Juanes">Juanes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Vives" title="Carlos Vives">Carlos Vives</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">[341]</a></sup> Colombian music blends European-influenced guitar and song structure with large <a href="/wiki/Gaita_flutes" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaita flutes">gaita flutes</a> and percussion instruments from the indigenous population, while its percussion structure and dance forms come from Africa. Colombia has a diverse and dynamic musical environment.<sup id="cite_ref-about.com_349-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about.com-349">[342]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Uribe_Holgu%C3%ADn" title="Guillermo Uribe Holguín">Guillermo Uribe Holguín</a>, an important cultural figure in the <a href="/wiki/National_Symphony_Orchestra_of_Colombia" title="National Symphony Orchestra of Colombia">National Symphony Orchestra of Colombia</a>, Luis Antonio Calvo and Blas Emilio Atehortúa are some of the greatest exponents of the <a href="/wiki/Art_music" title="Art music">art music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">[343]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Bogotá Philharmonic Orchestra">Bogotá Philharmonic Orchestra</a> is one of the most active orchestras in Colombia.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">[344]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Caribbean music has many vibrant rhythms, such as <a href="/wiki/Cumbia_(Colombia)" title="Cumbia (Colombia)">cumbia</a> (it is played by the <a href="/wiki/Maraca" title="Maraca">maracas</a>, the drums, the gaitas and <a href="/wiki/Guacharaca" title="Guacharaca">guacharaca</a>), <a href="/wiki/Porro" title="Porro">porro</a> (it is a monotonous but joyful rhythm), <a href="/wiki/Mapal%C3%A9" title="Mapalé">mapalé</a> (with its fast rhythm and constant <a href="/wiki/Clapping" title="Clapping">clapping</a>) and the "<a href="/wiki/Vallenato" title="Vallenato">vallenato</a>", which originated in the northern part of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> coast (the rhythm is mainly played by the caja, the guacharaca, and <a href="/wiki/Accordion" title="Accordion">accordion</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_music_352-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_music-352">[345]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">[346]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">[347]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">[348]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">[349]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Shakira_Stops_By_Soundcheck_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Shakira_Stops_By_Soundcheck_cropped.jpg/200px-Shakira_Stops_By_Soundcheck_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="249" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7e/Shakira_Stops_By_Soundcheck_cropped.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="262" data-file-height="326"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Shakira_Stops_By_Soundcheck_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Shakira" title="Shakira">Shakira</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The music from the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_coast" title="Pacific coast">Pacific coast</a>, such as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Currulao_(music_genre)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Currulao (music genre) (page does not exist)">currulao</a>, is characterized by its strong use of drums (instruments such as the native <a href="/wiki/Marimba" title="Marimba">marimba</a>, the conunos, the <a href="/wiki/Bass_drum" title="Bass drum">bass drum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Side_drum" class="mw-redirect" title="Side drum">side drum</a>, and the cuatro guasas or tubular rattle). An important rhythm of the south region of the Pacific coast is the <a href="/wiki/Contradanza" title="Contradanza">contradanza</a> (it is used in dance shows due to the striking colours of the costumes).<sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_music_352-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_music-352">[345]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">[350]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">[351]</a></sup> Marimba music, traditional chants and dances from the Colombia South Pacific region are on <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_Lists" title="UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage Lists">UNESCO's Representative List of the Intangible Cultural Heritage of Humanity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">[352]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">[353]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">[354]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Important musical rhythms of the <a href="/wiki/Andean_Region_(Colombia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Andean Region (Colombia)">Andean Region</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Danza" title="Danza">danza</a> (dance of Andean folklore arising from the transformation of the European contredance), the <a href="/wiki/Bambuco" title="Bambuco">bambuco</a> (it is played with guitar, <a href="/wiki/Colombian_tiple" title="Colombian tiple">tiple</a><sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">[355]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Mandolin" title="Mandolin">mandolin</a>, the rhythm is danced by couples), the <a href="/wiki/Pasillo" title="Pasillo">pasillo</a> (a rhythm inspired by the Austrian <a href="/wiki/Waltz" title="Waltz">waltz</a> and the Colombian "danza", the lyrics have been composed by well-known poets), the guabina (the <a href="/wiki/Tiple" title="Tiple">tiple</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bandola" title="Bandola">bandola</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Requinto" title="Requinto">requinto</a> are the basic instruments), the <a href="/wiki/Sanjuanero" title="Sanjuanero">sanjuanero</a> (it originated in <a href="/wiki/Tolima_Department" title="Tolima Department">Tolima</a> and <a href="/wiki/Huila_Department" title="Huila Department">Huila</a> Departments, the rhythm is joyful and fast).<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">[356]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">[357]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">[358]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">[359]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">[360]</a></sup> Apart from these traditional rhythms, <a href="/wiki/Salsa_music" title="Salsa music">salsa music</a> has spread throughout the country, and the city of <a href="/wiki/Cali" title="Cali">Cali</a> is considered by many salsa singers to be 'The New Salsa Capital of the World'.<sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_music_352-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_music-352">[345]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">[361]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">[362]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The instruments that distinguish the music of the <a href="/wiki/Orinoqu%C3%ADa_natural_region" title="Orinoquía natural region">Eastern Plains</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Harp" title="Harp">harp</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cuatro_(instrument)" title="Cuatro (instrument)">cuatro</a> (a type of four-stringed guitar) and maracas. Important rhythms of this region are the <a href="/wiki/Joropo" title="Joropo">joropo</a> (a fast rhythm and there is also tapping as a result of its <a href="/wiki/Flamenco" title="Flamenco">flamenco</a> ancestry) and the <a href="/wiki/Galeron" class="mw-redirect" title="Galeron">galeron</a> (it is heard a lot while <a href="/wiki/Cowboy" title="Cowboy">cowboys</a> are working).<sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_music_352-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_music-352">[345]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">[363]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">[364]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372">[365]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The music of the Amazon region is strongly influenced by the indigenous religious practices. Some of the musical instruments used are the manguaré (a musical instrument of <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial" class="mw-redirect" title="Ceremonial">ceremonial</a> type, consisting of a pair of large <a href="/wiki/Cylindrical_drum" title="Cylindrical drum">cylindrical drums</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Quena" title="Quena">quena</a> (melodic instrument), the <a href="/wiki/Rondador" title="Rondador">rondador</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Conga" title="Conga">congas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bell" title="Bell">bells</a>, and different types of flutes.<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">[366]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">[367]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">[368]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The music of the <a href="/wiki/Archipelago_of_San_Andr%C3%A9s,_Providencia_and_Santa_Catalina" title="Archipelago of San Andrés, Providencia and Santa Catalina">Archipelago of San Andrés, Providencia and Santa Catalina</a> is usually accompanied by a <a href="/wiki/Mandolin" title="Mandolin">mandolin</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Washtub_bass" title="Washtub bass">tub-bass</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Jawbone_(instrument)" title="Jawbone (instrument)">jawbone</a>, a guitar and <a href="/wiki/Maraca" title="Maraca">maracas</a>. Some popular archipelago rhythms are the <a href="/wiki/Schottische" title="Schottische">Schottische</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">Calypso</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Polka" title="Polka">Polka</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mento" title="Mento">Mento</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">[369]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">[370]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Popular_culture">Popular culture</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Theater_of_Colombia" title="Theater of Colombia">Theater of Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Colombia" title="Cinema of Colombia">Cinema of Colombia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Colombia">Media of Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Interior_Teatro_Colon_Bogota.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Interior_Teatro_Colon_Bogota.jpg/180px-Interior_Teatro_Colon_Bogota.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Interior_Teatro_Colon_Bogota.jpg/270px-Interior_Teatro_Colon_Bogota.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Interior_Teatro_Colon_Bogota.jpg/360px-Interior_Teatro_Colon_Bogota.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Interior_Teatro_Colon_Bogota.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Teatro Colón of Bogotá houses the Ibero-American Theater Festival of Bogotá, one of the biggest theater festivals in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Theater_Festival_378-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Theater_Festival-378">[371]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Theater was introduced in Colombia during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish colonization</a> in 1550 through <a href="/wiki/Zarzuela" title="Zarzuela">zarzuela</a> companies. Colombian theater is supported by the Ministry of Culture and a number of private and state owned organizations. The <a href="/wiki/Theater_of_Colombia" title="Theater of Colombia">Ibero-American Theater Festival of Bogotá</a> is the cultural event of the highest importance in Colombia and one of the biggest theater festivals in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Theater_Festival_378-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Theater_Festival-378">[371]</a></sup> Other important theater events are: The Festival of Puppet The Fanfare (Medellín), The Manizales Theater Festival, The Caribbean Theatre Festival (Santa Marta) and The Art Festival of Popular Culture "Cultural Invasion" (Bogotá).<sup id="cite_ref-Theatre_in_Colombia_379-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Theatre_in_Colombia-379">[372]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-theatrical_production_380-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theatrical_production-380">[373]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-teatro_siglo_XX_381-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teatro_siglo_XX-381">[374]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although the <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Colombia" title="Cinema of Colombia">Colombian cinema</a> is young as an industry, more recently the film industry was growing with support from the Film Act passed in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-the_Film_Act_passed_in_2003_382-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the_Film_Act_passed_in_2003-382">[375]</a></sup> Many film festivals take place in Colombia, but the two most important are the <a href="/wiki/Cartagena_Film_Festival" title="Cartagena Film Festival">Cartagena Film Festival</a>, which is the oldest film festival in Latin America, and the <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Film_Festival" title="Bogotá Film Festival">Bogotá Film Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fiapf_383-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fiapf-383">[376]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-film_festivals_384-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-film_festivals-384">[377]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-385" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-385">[378]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Statue_India_Catalina_FICCI.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Statue_India_Catalina_FICCI.JPG/200px-Statue_India_Catalina_FICCI.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Statue_India_Catalina_FICCI.JPG/300px-Statue_India_Catalina_FICCI.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Statue_India_Catalina_FICCI.JPG/400px-Statue_India_Catalina_FICCI.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1283"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Statue_India_Catalina_FICCI.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Cartagena_Film_Festival" title="Cartagena Film Festival">Cartagena Film Festival</a> is the oldest cinema event in Latin America. The central focus is on films from Ibero-America.<sup id="cite_ref-fiapf_383-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fiapf-383">[376]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Some important national circulation newspapers are <i><a href="/wiki/El_Tiempo_(Colombia)" title="El Tiempo (Colombia)">El Tiempo</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/El_Espectador" title="El Espectador">El Espectador</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Colombia" title="Television in Colombia">Television in Colombia</a> has two privately owned TV networks and three state-owned TV networks with national coverage, as well as six regional TV networks and dozens of local TV stations. Private channels, <a href="/wiki/RCN_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="RCN TV">RCN</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caracol_Televisi%C3%B3n" title="Caracol Televisión">Caracol</a> are the highest-rated. The regional channels and regional newspapers cover a department or more and its content is made in these particular areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Television_in_Colombia_386-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Television_in_Colombia-386">[379]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-press_387-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-press-387">[380]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_press_in_Colombia_388-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_press_in_Colombia-388">[381]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Colombia has three major national <a href="/wiki/Radio_in_Colombia" title="Radio in Colombia">radio networks</a>: <a href="/wiki/Radiodifusora_Nacional_de_Colombia" class="mw-redirect" title="Radiodifusora Nacional de Colombia">Radiodifusora Nacional de Colombia</a>, a state-run national radio; <a href="/wiki/Caracol_Radio" title="Caracol Radio">Caracol Radio</a> and <a href="/wiki/RCN_Radio" title="RCN Radio">RCN Radio</a>, privately owned networks with hundreds of affiliates. There are other national networks, including <a href="/wiki/Cadena_Super" class="mw-redirect" title="Cadena Super">Cadena Super</a>, <a href="/wiki/Todelar" title="Todelar">Todelar</a>, and Colmundo. Many hundreds of radio stations are registered with the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Information_Technologies_and_Communications_(Colombia)" title="Ministry of Information Technologies and Communications (Colombia)">Ministry of Information Technologies and Communications</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Radio_in_Colombia_389-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Radio_in_Colombia-389">[382]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Colombian_cuisine" title="Colombian cuisine">Colombian cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sancocho_de_gallina_criolla.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Sancocho_de_gallina_criolla.jpg/220px-Sancocho_de_gallina_criolla.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Sancocho_de_gallina_criolla.jpg/330px-Sancocho_de_gallina_criolla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Sancocho_de_gallina_criolla.jpg/440px-Sancocho_de_gallina_criolla.jpg 2x" data-file-width="630" data-file-height="320"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sancocho_de_gallina_criolla.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Sancocho de gallina criolla is a traditional soup in Colombia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Colombia's varied cuisine is influenced by its diverse fauna and flora as well as the cultural traditions of the ethnic groups. Colombian dishes and ingredients vary widely by region. Some of the most common ingredients are: cereals such as rice and maize; tubers such as potato and <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>; assorted <a href="/wiki/Legume" title="Legume">legumes</a>; meats, including beef, chicken, pork and goat; fish; and seafood.<sup id="cite_ref-Paseo_de_olla_390-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paseo_de_olla-390">[383]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-391">[384]</a></sup> Colombia cuisine also features a variety of tropical fruits such as <a href="/wiki/Physalis_peruviana" title="Physalis peruviana">cape gooseberry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acca_sellowiana" class="mw-redirect" title="Acca sellowiana">feijoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eugenia_stipitata" title="Eugenia stipitata">arazá</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pitaya" title="Pitaya">dragon fruit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Purple_mangosteen" class="mw-redirect" title="Purple mangosteen">mangostino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Passiflora_ligularis" title="Passiflora ligularis">granadilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papaya" title="Papaya">papaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guava" title="Guava">guava</a>, mora (<a href="/wiki/Blackberry" title="Blackberry">blackberry</a>), <a href="/wiki/Solanum_quitoense" title="Solanum quitoense">lulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annona_muricata" class="mw-redirect" title="Annona muricata">soursop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Passionfruit" class="mw-redirect" title="Passionfruit">passionfruit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_cuisine_392-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_cuisine-392">[385]</a></sup> Colombia is one of the world's largest consumers of fruit juices.<sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">[386]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Among the most representative appetizers and soups are <a href="/wiki/Tostones" title="Tostones">patacones</a> (fried green plantains), <a href="/wiki/Sancocho" title="Sancocho">sancocho</a> de gallina (chicken soup with root vegetables) and <a href="/wiki/Ajiaco" title="Ajiaco">ajiaco</a> (potato and corn soup). Representative snacks and breads are <a href="/wiki/Pandebono" title="Pandebono">pandebono</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arepa" title="Arepa">arepas</a> (corn cakes), <a href="/wiki/Aborrajado" class="mw-redirect" title="Aborrajado">aborrajados</a> (fried sweet plantains with cheese), <a href="/wiki/Torta" title="Torta">torta</a> de <a href="/wiki/Choclo" class="mw-redirect" title="Choclo">choclo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Empanada" title="Empanada">empanadas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Almoj%C3%A1bana" title="Almojábana">almojábanas</a>. Representative main courses are <a href="/wiki/Bandeja_paisa" title="Bandeja paisa">bandeja paisa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lechona_tolimense" class="mw-redirect" title="Lechona tolimense">lechona tolimense</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ternera_a_la_llanera" class="mw-redirect" title="Ternera a la llanera">mamona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamales" class="mw-redirect" title="Tamales">tamales</a> and fish dishes (such as <a href="/wiki/Arroz_de_lisa" title="Arroz de lisa">arroz de lisa</a>), especially in coastal regions where <a href="/wiki/Kibbeh" title="Kibbeh">kibbeh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suero" title="Suero">suero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coste%C3%B1o_cheese" title="Costeño cheese">costeño cheese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carima%C3%B1ola" title="Carimañola">carimañolas</a> are also eaten. Representative side dishes are papas chorreadas (potatoes with cheese), remolachas rellenas con huevo duro (beets stuffed with <a href="/wiki/Hard-boiled_egg" class="mw-redirect" title="Hard-boiled egg">hard-boiled egg</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Coconut_rice" title="Coconut rice">arroz con coco</a> (coconut rice).<sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_cuisine_392-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_cuisine-392">[385]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Paseo_de_olla_390-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paseo_de_olla-390">[383]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Organic_food" title="Organic food">Organic food</a> is a current trend in big cities, although in general across the country the fruits and veggies are very natural and fresh.<sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-394">[387]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_Food_395-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_Food-395">[388]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Representative desserts are <a href="/wiki/Bu%C3%B1uelo" title="Buñuelo">buñuelos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Natilla">natillas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Luisa_cake" title="Maria Luisa cake">Maria Luisa cake</a>, bocadillo made of guayaba (<a href="/wiki/Guava_jelly" title="Guava jelly">guava jelly</a>), <a href="/wiki/Cocadas" class="mw-redirect" title="Cocadas">cocadas</a> (coconut balls), casquitos de guayaba (candied guava peels), <a href="/wiki/Torta_de_nata" title="Torta de nata">torta de natas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oblea" title="Oblea">obleas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cr%C3%A8me_caramel" title="Crème caramel">flan</a> de <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mango</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rosc%C3%B3n" title="Roscón">roscón</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milhoja" title="Milhoja">milhoja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manjar_blanco" title="Manjar blanco">manjar blanco</a>, dulce de <a href="/wiki/Feijoa" class="mw-redirect" title="Feijoa">feijoa</a>, dulce de <a href="/wiki/Mountain_papaya" title="Mountain papaya">papayuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Torta" title="Torta">torta</a> de mojicón, and esponjado de <a href="/wiki/Curuba" class="mw-redirect" title="Curuba">curuba</a>. Typical sauces (salsas) are <a href="/wiki/Hogao" title="Hogao">hogao</a> (tomato and onion sauce) and Colombian-style <a href="/wiki/Aj%C3%AD_(sauce)" title="Ají (sauce)">ají</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_cuisine_392-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_cuisine-392">[385]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Paseo_de_olla_390-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paseo_de_olla-390">[383]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Some representative beverages are <a href="/wiki/Coffee_production_in_Colombia" title="Coffee production in Colombia">coffee</a> (Tinto), <a href="/wiki/Champ%C3%BAs" title="Champús">champús</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cholado" title="Cholado">cholado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lulada" title="Lulada">lulada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avena_(beverage)" class="mw-redirect" title="Avena (beverage)">avena</a> colombiana, <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> juice, <a href="/wiki/Aguapanela" title="Aguapanela">aguapanela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aguardiente" title="Aguardiente">aguardiente</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hot_chocolate" title="Hot chocolate">hot chocolate</a> and fresh fruit juices (often made with water or milk).<sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_cuisine_392-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_cuisine-392">[385]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Paseo_de_olla_390-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paseo_de_olla-390">[383]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Colombia" title="Sport in Colombia">Sport in Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nairo_Quintana,_Paris-Nice_2013.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Nairo_Quintana%2C_Paris-Nice_2013.JPG/220px-Nairo_Quintana%2C_Paris-Nice_2013.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Nairo_Quintana%2C_Paris-Nice_2013.JPG/330px-Nairo_Quintana%2C_Paris-Nice_2013.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Nairo_Quintana%2C_Paris-Nice_2013.JPG/440px-Nairo_Quintana%2C_Paris-Nice_2013.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1065"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nairo_Quintana,_Paris-Nice_2013.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Nairo_Quintana" title="Nairo Quintana">Nairo Quintana</a>: Colombian Champion of the <a href="/wiki/Giro_d%27Italia" title="Giro d'Italia">Giro d'Italia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vuelta_a_Espa%C3%B1a" title="Vuelta a España">Vuelta a España</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tejo_(sport)" title="Tejo (sport)">Tejo</a> is Colombia's national sport and is a team sport that involves launching projectiles to hit a target.<sup id="cite_ref-Tejo-Colombia's_national_sport._396-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tejo-Colombia's_national_sport.-396">[389]</a></sup> But of all sports in Colombia, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> is the most popular. <a href="/wiki/Colombia_national_football_team" title="Colombia national football team">Colombia</a> was the champion of the <a href="/wiki/2001_Copa_Am%C3%A9rica" title="2001 Copa América">2001 Copa América</a>, in which they set a new record of being undefeated, conceding no goals and winning each match. Colombia has been awarded "<a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings#Best_Mover_of_the_Year" title="FIFA World Rankings">mover of the year</a>" twice.<sup id="cite_ref-397" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-397">[390]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Colombia is a hub for <a href="/wiki/Inline_speed_skating" title="Inline speed skating">roller skaters</a>. The national team is a perennial powerhouse at the World Roller Speed Skating Championships.<sup id="cite_ref-Patinaje_colombiano_398-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Patinaje_colombiano-398">[391]</a></sup> Colombia has traditionally been very good in <a href="/wiki/Cycle_sport" title="Cycle sport">cycling</a> and a large number of Colombian cyclists have triumphed in major competitions of cycling.<sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_cycling_399-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_cycling-399">[392]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Baseball is popular in cities like <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Colombia" title="Cartagena, Colombia">Cartagena</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barranquilla" title="Barranquilla">Barranquilla</a>. Of those cities have come good players like: <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Cabrera" title="Orlando Cabrera">Orlando Cabrera</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89dgar_Renter%C3%ADa" title="Édgar Rentería">Édgar Rentería</a>, who was champion of the <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> in <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Series" title="1997 World Series">1997</a> and <a href="/wiki/2010_World_Series" title="2010 World Series">2010</a><sup id="cite_ref-400" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-400">[393]</a></sup> and others who have played in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>. Colombia was <a href="/wiki/Baseball_World_Cup" title="Baseball World Cup">world amateur champion</a> in 1947 and 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-béisbolglorias_401-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-béisbolglorias-401">[394]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">Boxing</a> is one of the sports that has produced more world champions for Colombia.<sup id="cite_ref-History_of_boxing_402-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_boxing-402">[395]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Boxing_champions_403-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boxing_champions-403">[396]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Motorsport" title="Motorsport">Motorsports</a> also occupies an important place in the sporting preferences of Colombians; <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pablo_Montoya" title="Juan Pablo Montoya">Juan Pablo Montoya</a> is a race car driver known for winning 7 Formula One events. Colombia also has excelled in sports such as <a href="/wiki/UCI_BMX_World_Championships" title="UCI BMX World Championships">BMX</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shooting_sport" class="mw-redirect" title="Shooting sport">shooting sport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">taekwondo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wrestling" title="Wrestling">wrestling</a>, <a href="/wiki/High_diving" title="High diving">high diving</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sport_of_athletics" title="Sport of athletics">athletics</a>, also has a long tradition in <a href="/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting" title="Olympic weightlifting">weightlifting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bowling" title="Bowling">bowling</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-404" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-404">[397]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-405" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-405">[398]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-406" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-406">[399]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_care_in_Colombia" title="Health care in Colombia">Health care in Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Complejo_M%C3%A9dico_-_Hospital_Internacional_de_Colombia_HIC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Complejo_M%C3%A9dico_-_Hospital_Internacional_de_Colombia_HIC.jpg/220px-Complejo_M%C3%A9dico_-_Hospital_Internacional_de_Colombia_HIC.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Complejo_M%C3%A9dico_-_Hospital_Internacional_de_Colombia_HIC.jpg/330px-Complejo_M%C3%A9dico_-_Hospital_Internacional_de_Colombia_HIC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Complejo_M%C3%A9dico_-_Hospital_Internacional_de_Colombia_HIC.jpg/440px-Complejo_M%C3%A9dico_-_Hospital_Internacional_de_Colombia_HIC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3992" data-file-height="2242"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Complejo_M%C3%A9dico_-_Hospital_Internacional_de_Colombia_HIC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
