         </div>Colombia leads the annual <i><a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A9rica_Econom%C3%ADa" title="América Economía">América Economía</a></i> ranking of the best clinics and hospitals in Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_clinics_407-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_clinics-407">[400]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The overall <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> in Colombia at birth is 74.8 years (71.2 years for males and 78.4 years for females).<sup id="cite_ref-Life_expectancy_at_birth_262-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Life_expectancy_at_birth-262">[255]</a></sup> Healthcare reforms have led to massive improvements in the healthcare systems of the country, with health standards in Colombia improving very much since the 1980s. Although this new system has widened population coverage by the social and health security system from 21% (pre-1993) to 96% in 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-408" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-408">[401]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Health_equity" title="Health equity">health disparities</a> persist. </p>
      <p>Through <a href="/wiki/Medical_tourism" title="Medical tourism">health tourism</a>, many people from over the world travel from their places of residence to other countries in search of medical treatment and the attractions in the countries visited. Colombia is projected as one of Latin America's main destinations in terms of health tourism due to the quality of its <a href="/wiki/Health_care_professional" class="mw-redirect" title="Health care professional">health care professionals</a>, a good number of institutions devoted to health, and an immense inventory of natural and architectural sites. Cities such as Bogotá, Cali, Medellín and Bucaramanga are the most visited in <a href="/wiki/Cardiology" title="Cardiology">cardiology</a> procedures, <a href="/wiki/Neurology" title="Neurology">neurology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dental_treatment" class="mw-redirect" title="Dental treatment">dental treatments</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stem_cell_therapy" class="mw-redirect" title="Stem cell therapy">stem cell therapy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Otorhinolaryngology" title="Otorhinolaryngology">ENT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ophthalmology" title="Ophthalmology">ophthalmology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joint_replacement" title="Joint replacement">joint replacements</a> because of the quality of medical treatment.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>A study conducted by <i><a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A9rica_Econom%C3%ADa" title="América Economía">América Economía</a></i> magazine ranked 21 Colombian <a href="/wiki/Health_facility" title="Health facility">health care institutions</a> among the top 44 in Latin America, amounting to 48 percent of the total.<sup id="cite_ref-Colombian_clinics_407-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colombian_clinics-407">[400]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Cancer_research" title="Cancer research">cancer research</a> and treatment centre was declared as a Project of National Strategic Interest.<sup id="cite_ref-409" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-409">[402]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Colombia" title="Education in Colombia">Education in Colombia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:UNAL-Bloque_M5-Facultad_de_Minas-Medellin2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/UNAL-Bloque_M5-Facultad_de_Minas-Medellin2.JPG/200px-UNAL-Bloque_M5-Facultad_de_Minas-Medellin2.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/UNAL-Bloque_M5-Facultad_de_Minas-Medellin2.JPG/300px-UNAL-Bloque_M5-Facultad_de_Minas-Medellin2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/UNAL-Bloque_M5-Facultad_de_Minas-Medellin2.JPG/400px-UNAL-Bloque_M5-Facultad_de_Minas-Medellin2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:UNAL-Bloque_M5-Facultad_de_Minas-Medellin2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>M5 building – <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Colombia" title="National University of Colombia">National University of Colombia</a>, designed by <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Nel_G%C3%B3mez" title="Pedro Nel Gómez">Pedro Nel Gómez</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Universidad_de_los_Andes_(3326108271).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Universidad_de_los_Andes_%283326108271%29.jpg/200px-Universidad_de_los_Andes_%283326108271%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Universidad_de_los_Andes_%283326108271%29.jpg/300px-Universidad_de_los_Andes_%283326108271%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Universidad_de_los_Andes_%283326108271%29.jpg/400px-Universidad_de_los_Andes_%283326108271%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Universidad_de_los_Andes_(3326108271).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mario Laserna Building – <a href="/wiki/University_of_Los_Andes_(Colombia)" title="University of Los Andes (Colombia)">University of Los Andes</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The educational experience of many Colombian children begins with attendance at a <a href="/wiki/Preschool" title="Preschool">preschool</a> academy until age five (<i>Educación preescolar</i>). Basic education (<i>Educación básica</i>) is compulsory by law.<sup id="cite_ref-410" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-410">[403]</a></sup> It has two stages: Primary basic education (<i>Educación básica primaria</i>) which goes from first to fifth grade – children from six to ten years old, and Secondary basic education (<i>Educación básica secundaria</i>), which goes from sixth to ninth grade. Basic education is followed by Middle vocational education (<i>Educación media vocacional</i>) that comprises the tenth and eleventh grades. It may have different vocational training modalities or specialties (academic, technical, business, and so on.) according to the curriculum adopted by each school.<sup id="cite_ref-sistema_educativo_411-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sistema_educativo-411">[404]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the successful completion of all the basic and middle education years, a <a href="/wiki/High-school_diploma" class="mw-redirect" title="High-school diploma">high-school diploma</a> is awarded. The high-school graduate is known as a <i>bachiller</i>, because secondary basic school and middle education are traditionally considered together as a unit called <i>bachillerato</i> (sixth to eleventh grade). Students in their final year of middle education take the <a href="/wiki/ICFES_Examination" class="mw-redirect" title="ICFES Examination">ICFES test</a> (now renamed Saber 11) to gain access to higher education (<i>Educación superior</i>). This higher education includes undergraduate professional studies, technical, technological and intermediate professional education, and post-graduate studies. Technical professional institutions of Higher Education are also opened to students holder of a qualification in Arts and Business. This qualification is usually awarded by the <a href="/wiki/National_Service_of_Learning_(Colombia)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Service of Learning (Colombia)">SENA</a> after a two years curriculum.<sup id="cite_ref-412" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-412">[405]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><i>Bachilleres</i> (high-school graduates) may enter into a professional undergraduate career program offered by a university; these programs last up to five years (or less for technical, technological and intermediate professional education, and post-graduate studies), even as much to six to seven years for some careers, such as medicine. In Colombia, there is not an institution such as college; students go directly into a career program at a university or any other educational institution to obtain a professional, technical or technological title. Once graduated from the university, people are granted a (professional, technical or technological) diploma and licensed (if required) to practice the career they have chosen. For some professional career programs, students are required to take the Saber-Pro test, in their final year of undergraduate academic education.<sup id="cite_ref-sistema_educativo_411-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sistema_educativo-411">[404]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Public spending on education as a proportion of gross domestic product in 2015 was 4.49%. This represented 15.05% of total government expenditure. The <a href="/wiki/Gross_enrolment_ratio" title="Gross enrolment ratio">primary and secondary gross enrolment ratios</a> stood at 113.56% and 98.09% respectively. <a href="/wiki/School-life_expectancy" class="mw-redirect" title="School-life expectancy">School-life expectancy</a> was 14.42 years. A total of 94.58% of the population aged 15 and older were recorded as literate, including 98.66% of those aged 15–24.<sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO_264-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO-264">[257]</a></sup> </p>

        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">(<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Es-republica_de_colombia.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ed/Es-republica_de_colombia.ogg" class="internal" title="Es-republica de colombia.ogg"><i class="unicode" lang="es">República de Colombia</i></a></span>&nbsp;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Es-republica_de_colombia.ogg" title="File:Es-republica de colombia.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[Note 1]</a></sup></span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1011085734">
      <div class="reflist"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">IPA transcription of "<i>República de Colombia</i>": <small>Spanish pronunciation:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[reˈpuβlika ðe koˈlombja]</a></span>.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Balboa is best known for being the first European to see the Pacific Ocean in 1513, which he called <i>Mar del Sur</i> (or "Sea of the South") and would facilitate Spanish exploration and settlement of South America.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-59"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-59">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A royal decree of 1713 approved the legality of <a href="/wiki/Palenque_de_San_Basilio" class="mw-redirect" title="Palenque de San Basilio">Palenque de San Basilio</a> founded by runaway slaves as a refuge in the seventeenth century. The people of San Basilio fought against slavery, thereby giving rise to the first free place in the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup> Its main leader was <a href="/wiki/Benkos_Bioho" class="mw-redirect" title="Benkos Bioho">Benkos Biohó</a>, who was born in West Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[55]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-62">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Peter_Claver" title="Peter Claver">Peter Claver</a> was a Spaniard who traveled to Cartagena in 1610 and was ordained as a <a href="/wiki/Jesuit" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesuit">Jesuit</a> priest in 1616. Claver cared for African slaves for thirty-eight years, defending their lives and the <a href="/wiki/Dignity" title="Dignity">dignity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[57]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-116"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-116">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9ctor_Abad_G%C3%B3mez" title="Héctor Abad Gómez">Héctor Abad</a> was a prominent medical doctor, university professor, and human rights leader whose holistic vision of healthcare led him to found the Colombian National School of Public Health. The increasing violence and human rights abuses of the 1970s and 1980s led him to fight for social justice in his community.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[110]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-118"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-118">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Javier_de_Nicol%C3%B3" title="Javier de Nicoló">Javier de Nicoló</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Salesian" class="mw-redirect" title="Salesian">Salesian</a> priest who grew up in war-torn Italy and arrived in Colombia a year after the bogotazo. He developed a program that has offered more than 40,000 young people the education and moral support they needed to become productive citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[111]</a></sup></span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
